{"uri": "8220349681", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-11", "time": "11:25:38", "dateTime": "2024-07-11T11:25:38Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-11T11:23:27Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.8470588326454163, "url": "https://tribune.com.pk/story/2478822/learning-from-the-1995-srebrenica-tragedy-could-have-prevented-gaza-genocide-turkish-official", "title": "Learning from the 1995 Srebrenica tragedy could have prevented Gaza genocide: Turkish official", "body": "If humanity learned a lesson from the Srebrenica genocide, which took place 29 years ago in eastern Bosnia, the genocide in Gaza would not have happened today, the Turkish communications director said on Thursday.\n\n\"If humanity had truly learned from the harrowing events in Srebrenica, where over 8,000 people were killed solely because of their identities and beliefs without making any distinction between the young and the old, the genocide in Gaza would not have taken place today,\" Fahrettin Altun said on X.\n\nAmid the \"relentless genocide\" happening in Gaza, there are valuable lessons for all to learn from Srebrenica, urging people to strive for a livable world where human dignity is cherished and preserved, he said.\n\nHe recalled the words of the first President of Bosnia and Herzegovina, Aliya Izetbegovic: \"A forgotten genocide is repeated.\" The July 11 Srebrenica Genocide is \"one of the most painful chapters in modern history that has yet to be closed,\" Altun also said.\n\nHe stressed that a \"horrifying genocide\" unfolded before the eyes of the entire world in an area designated as a \"safe zone\" by the UN in Srebrenica.\n\n\"Ratko Mladic, etched in history as the 'Butcher of Bosnia,' like those who perpetuate the genocide in Gaza today, was tragically blinded by ideology and ignored the pleas of reason, common sense, and conscience,\" he added.\n\nUnderlining that the UN General Assembly adopted the Srebrenica Genocide Resolution with the support of T\u00fcrkiye in May, he said this resolution mandates that Srebrenica be taught to younger generations worldwide as a lesson.\n\nA circular signed by Turkish President Recep Tayyip Erdogan designates July 11 in T\u00fcrkiye as the International Day of Reflection and Commemoration of the Srebrenica Genocide.\n\n\"This day aims to share the profound pain and to condemn genocide and crimes against humanity. We hope that this tragic event will deepen humanity's conscience and awareness and awaken dormant consciences to the genocide unfolding in Gaza before the eyes of the entire world,\" he said.\n\nHe added that the bodies of 14 more victims will be laid to rest at this year's mass funeral on July 11.\n\n\"I pray for Allah's mercy upon the Bosnian War victims who were massacred throughout brotherly Bosnia and Herzegovina, particularly those who endured genocide in Srebrenica, all Bosnian martyrs, and Aliya Izetbegovic, the first President of the Independent Bosnia and Herzegovina, who showed the world that even war has its ethics,\" he added.\n\nEvery year on July 11, newly identified victims of the 1995 genocide are buried in a memorial cemetery in Potocari in Bosnia and Herzegovina.\n\nNewly Identified Victims Laid to Rest\n\nThis May, with overwhelming support, the UN General Assembly passed a resolution designating July 11 Srebrenica Genocide Remembrance Day.\n\nThe resolution, spearheaded by Germany and co-sponsored by more than 40 countries, calls for July 11 to be declared as the International Day of Reflection and Commemoration of the 1995 Genocide in Srebrenica.\n\nThe youngest victim to be buried this year is Beriz Mujic, 17, born in 1978 in Zvornik.\n\nHis remains were found 28 years after he was killed and were exhumed in May 2023.\n\nHe was killed in July 1995 in the Suceska area near Bratunac, and his remains were discovered and exhumed in the Srebrenica municipality area.\n\nMujic will be buried next to his brother Hazim, whose remains were laid to rest in 2013.\n\nThe body of their father, Omer Mujic, has yet to be found.\n\nThe oldest victim to be buried Thursday is Hamed Salic, born in 1927. He was 68 when he went missing in the summer of 1995 in the town of Zepa. His remains were exhumed in May 2014 and recently identified.\n\nThousands of people from various countries will attend the funerals and burials. Following this year's funeral, the number of victims buried at the cemetery will reach 6,765.\n\nSrebrenica Genocide\n\nIn the spring of 1993, the UN Security Council declared the city of Srebrenica a \"safe area.\" However, Serb troops led by Gen. Ratko Mladic, who was later found guilty of war crimes, crimes against humanity, and genocide, overran the zone.\n\nDutch troops responsible for safeguarding people in the UN zone failed to act when Serb forces occupied it on July 11, killing 2,000 men and boys in a single day.\n\nApproximately 15,000 Bosniaks fled to the surrounding mountains, but Serb troops hunted them down, killing an additional 6,000 people.\n\nSerb forces allowed women and children to reach Bosnian-controlled regions but massacred at least 8,372 Bosnian men in forests, factories, and warehouses. The murdered Bosnians were buried in mass graves, with bodies discovered in 570 different locations across the country, including 77 mass graves.\n\nIn 2007, the International Court of Justice in The Hague ruled that genocide had been committed in Srebrenica.\n\nEfforts to locate the missing victims of the genocide have continued, with identified remains buried at the Potocari Memorial Cemetery.\n\nOn June 8, 2021, UN tribunal judges upheld a life sentence for Mladic for genocide, persecution, crimes against humanity, extermination, and other war crimes committed in Bosnia and T\u00fcrkiye's Communications Director Fahrettin Altun\n\nIf humanity learned a lesson from the Srebrenica genocide, which took place 29 years ago in eastern Bosnia, the genocide in Gaza would not have happened today, the Turkish communications director said on Thursday.\n\n\"If humanity had truly learned from the harrowing events in Srebrenica, where over 8,000 people were killed solely because of their identities and beliefs without making any distinction between the young and the old, the genocide in Gaza would not have taken place today,\" Fahrettin Altun said on X.\n\nAmid the \"relentless genocide\" happening in Gaza, there are valuable lessons for all to learn from Srebrenica, urging people to strive for a livable world where human dignity is cherished and preserved, he said.\n\nHe recalled the words of the first President of Bosnia and Herzegovina, Aliya Izetbegovic: \"A forgotten genocide is repeated.\" The July 11 Srebrenica Genocide is \"one of the most painful chapters in modern history that has yet to be closed,\" Altun also said.\n\nHe stressed that a \"horrifying genocide\" unfolded before the eyes of the entire world in an area designated as a \"safe zone\" by the UN in Srebrenica.\n\n\"Ratko Mladic, etched in history as the 'Butcher of Bosnia,' like those who perpetuate the genocide in Gaza today, was tragically blinded by ideology and ignored the pleas of reason, common sense, and conscience,\" he added.\n\nUnderlining that the UN General Assembly adopted the Srebrenica Genocide Resolution with the support of T\u00fcrkiye in May, he said this resolution mandates that Srebrenica be taught to younger generations worldwide as a lesson.\n\nA circular signed by Turkish President Recep Tayyip Erdogan designates July 11 in T\u00fcrkiye as the International Day of Reflection and Commemoration of the Srebrenica Genocide.\n\n\"This day aims to share the profound pain and to condemn genocide and crimes against humanity. We hope that this tragic event will deepen humanity's conscience and awareness and awaken dormant consciences to the genocide unfolding in Gaza before the eyes of the entire world,\" he said.\n\nHe added that the bodies of 14 more victims will be laid to rest at this year's mass funeral on July 11.\n\n\"I pray for Allah's mercy upon the Bosnian War victims who were massacred throughout brotherly Bosnia and Herzegovina, particularly those who endured genocide in Srebrenica, all Bosnian martyrs, and Aliya Izetbegovic, the first President of the Independent Bosnia and Herzegovina, who showed the world that even war has its ethics,\" he added.\n\nEvery year on July 11, newly identified victims of the 1995 genocide are buried in a memorial cemetery in Potocari in Bosnia and Herzegovina.\n\nThis May, with overwhelming support, the UN General Assembly passed a resolution designating July 11 Srebrenica Genocide Remembrance Day.\n\nThe resolution, spearheaded by Germany and co-sponsored by more than 40 countries, calls for July 11 to be declared as the International Day of Reflection and Commemoration of the 1995 Genocide in Srebrenica.\n\nThe youngest victim to be buried this year is Beriz Mujic, 17, born in 1978 in Zvornik.\n\nHis remains were found 28 years after he was killed and were exhumed in May 2023.\n\nHe was killed in July 1995 in the Suceska area near Bratunac, and his remains were discovered and exhumed in the Srebrenica municipality area.\n\nMujic will be buried next to his brother Hazim, whose remains were laid to rest in 2013.\n\nThe body of their father, Omer Mujic, has yet to be found.\n\nThe oldest victim to be buried Thursday is Hamed Salic, born in 1927. He was 68 when he went missing in the summer of 1995 in the town of Zepa. His remains were exhumed in May 2014 and recently identified.\n\nThousands of people from various countries will attend the funerals and burials. Following this year's funeral, the number of victims buried at the cemetery will reach 6,765.\n\nIn the spring of 1993, the UN Security Council declared the city of Srebrenica a \"safe area.\" However, Serb troops led by Gen. Ratko Mladic, who was later found guilty of war crimes, crimes against humanity, and genocide, overran the zone.\n\nDutch troops responsible for safeguarding people in the UN zone failed to act when Serb forces occupied it on July 11, killing 2,000 men and boys in a single day.\n\nApproximately 15,000 Bosniaks fled to the surrounding mountains, but Serb troops hunted them down, killing an additional 6,000 people.\n\nSerb forces allowed women and children to reach Bosnian-controlled regions but massacred at least 8,372 Bosnian men in forests, factories, and warehouses. {"uri": "8220230494", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-11", "time": "10:15:45", "dateTime": "2024-07-11T10:15:45Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-11T10:14:42Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.8274509906768799, "url": "https://www.yenisafak.com/en/news/bosnia-marks-29th-anniversary-of-srebrenica-genocide-3687351", "title": "Bosnia marks 29th anniversary of Srebrenica genocide | Politics", "body": "14 more newly identified victims of Srebrenica genocide to be laid to rest in memorial cemetery in village of Potocari\n\nBosnia and Herzegovina marked the 29th anniversary of the Srebrenica genocide Thursday in the wake of several developments since the killing of more than 8,000 civilians in July 1995, including the sentencing of 45 of those responsible for the atrocity to nearly 700 years in prison.\n\nOn Dec. 21, 1991, Bosnian Serbs proclaimed their own republic after voting against independence from Yugoslavia in a referendum.\n\nOn Jan. 9, 1992, they proclaimed the Republic of the Serbian People in Bosnia-Herzegovina but did not officially declare independence.\n\nThe war lasted until Dec. 14, 1995, and more than 100,000 people were killed and 2 million had to migrate.\n\nThe UN Security Council in the spring of 1993 declared Srebrenica a \"safe area.\" But Serb troops led by Gen. Ratko Mladic - who was later found guilty of war crimes, crimes against humanity and genocide - overran the UN zone.\n\nThe fate of approximately 7,000 people who disappeared during the war is still unknown.\n\nRadovan Karadzic, the leader of the Bosnian Serbs during the Bosnian War, was sentenced to 40 years in prison for many crimes, including the Srebrenica Genocide, and then to life imprisonment in an appeal case.\n\nIn the Srebrenica cases heard at the ICTY, former Serbian officials Ljubisa Beara and Vujadin Popovic were also sentenced to life imprisonment.\n\nIn its decision in 2007, the International Court of Justice in The Hague described what happened in Srebrenica and its surroundings as a \"genocide,\" based on evidence from the ICTY.\n\nIn the Srebrenica cases heard at the ICTY, Drago Nikolic was sentenced to 35 years in prison, Radislav Krstic to 35 years, Radivoje Miletic to 19 years, Ljubomir Borovcanin to 17 years, Vidoje Blagojevic to 15 years, Vinko Pandurevic to 13 years and Milan Gvero to five years.\n\nIn a case at the Court of Bosnia and Herzegovina, Milorad Trbic was found guilty of genocide and was sentenced to 30 years in prison for his part in the killing of nearly 1,000 Bosnian civilians in July 1995.\n\nTo date, 45 Serbs have been sentenced to a total of 699 years in prison in cases heard in different courts.\n\nMost of the Bosnian male civilians who took shelter in a battery factory used as a base by Dutch UN soldiers were killed by Serbs there.\n\nDespite the passing of years, the role of Dutch UN soldiers in the genocide continued to be debated.\n\nIn images taken after the occupation of Srebrenica, Dutch commander Thom Karremans was seen meeting with Mladic on July 11, 1995. It was noted that Mladic bought Karremans a drink at the end of the footage and the two toasted together.\n\nWhile Karremans was never tried for what happened, the Dutch state was found \"partially\" guilty of the genocide in Srebrenica.\n\nFormer Defense Minister Kajsa Ollongren offered the apology at the 27th commemoration of the genocide at the cemetery in the village of Potocari in Bosnia and Herzegovina.\n\n''Despite everything, Srebrenica was crushed...The Netherlands is also a part of this failure. For this reason, we offer you our deepest apologies,'' said Ollongren.\n\nShe said international institutions had promised to protect innocent people.\n\nIn a lawsuit filed in 2007 by relatives of the victims against the Dutch government, The Hague District Court found The Netherlands guilty of handing over 300 Bosniak civilians to the Serbs who had taken refuge with Dutch soldiers and the United Nations during the occupation of Srebrenica.\n\n- UN resolution commemorating genocide\n\nThe UN in late May this year passed a resolution to designate July 11 as the \"International Day of Reflection and Commemoration of the 1995 Genocide in Srebrenica\" with overwhelming support from the General Assembly.\n\nIt passed with 84 nations voting in favor and 19 against. A total of 68 countries abstained.\n\nCondemning the denial of the Srebrenica genocide, the resolution denounced the glorification of crimes against humanity, genocide and war criminals.\n\nHighlighting the importance of ongoing efforts for the identification of victims and the retrieval of bodies, the resolution emphasizes the need for all perpetrators to be brought to justice.\n\nSerbian President Aleksandar Vucic argued before the vote that the resolution was \"highly politicized.\"\n\nAccusing Germany of threatening countries that did not support the resolution, Vucic said: \"Is that European values, democratic values?\"\n\nWhile not legally binding, General Assembly resolutions carry political weight and send a strong message to the international community.\n\nT\u00fcrkiye has officially declared July 11 as the \"International Day of Reflection and Remembrance of the Srebrenica Genocide,\" according to a presidential decree published in the Official Gazette on Wednesday.\n\n\"July 11, accepted as the 'International Day of Reflection and Remembrance of the Srebrenica Genocide,' will be commemorated in our country to share the pain, condemn genocide and crimes against humanity, and raise global awareness through special remembrance events, educational activities and public awareness initiatives in honor of the victims of the Srebrenica genocide,\" it added.\n\nKosovo is another country that decided Wednesday to declare July 11 Srebrenica genocide remembrance day to honor the memory of the victims.\n\n- Serbia apologizes\n\nIn 2017, then-Serbian President Tomislav Nikolic apologized for all \"crimes\" committed by Serbs during the break-up of Yugoslavia, including Srebrenica.\n\nBut he refused to call the killing of thousands of Bosnian Muslims an act of genocide.\n\nSerbia has never accepted the killings as genocide.\n\nNikolic said he was kneeling and seeking forgiveness for Srebrenica.\n\nIn 2015, then-Prime Minister Aleksandar Vucic attended the commemoration ceremony on July 11 and paid respect to the victims. However, he quickly left the ceremony after being attacked by a stone-throwing mob.\n\nHe was forced to flee with his bodyguards on July 11, 2015 under a hail of stones thrown by mourners at a funeral prayer and burial service for 136 Srebrenica victims whose remains were recently discovered.\n\nPeople from the Bosnian village of Potocari - the scene of the genocide of Bosnian Muslim men and boys in 1995 - shouted \"Justice!\" and \"Vucic leave!\" as the Serbian premier was immediately forced to leave the cemetery.\n\nHe said he was given a warm welcome by the victims' families and the Bosniak mayor of Srebrenica, Camil Durakovic, upon his arrival at the memorial and cemetery complex, adding he refused to hide, despite hearing slogans demanding that he be \"shot.\"\n\n\"I was physically attacked as I was proceeding to the designated seating area, and my glasses fell off my face and broke,\" Vucic said. \"I am sorry that such an incident occurred and some people did not respond to our intention of building a friendship between Bosnians and Serbs.\"\n\n\"I am the one who extends his hand to you and wants to have peace with you. This is our policy,\" he said.\n\nVucic also urged the Serbian people \"to not raise their hands to anyone, thinking they can do anything they want,\" as \"we have to live together with the Bosniaks in the future too.\"\n\n- Council of Europe: Serbia must recognize 1995 genocide\n\nA Council of Europe body in 2017 called on Serbia to officially recognize the 1995 Srebrenica massacre as a genocide and to punish those responsible.\n\nIt said Belgrade should \"actively implement\" a strategy to punish those guilty of war crimes.\n\n- Srebrenica genocide denier awarded Nobel medal\n\nIn 2019, the Swedish Academy picked a 77-year-old Austrian author, Peter Handke, for the Nobel Prize in literature, despite his denial of the Srebrenica genocide.\n\nThe academy's choice was met with backlash worldwide.\n\nHandke claimed that Muslim Bosniaks in Sarajevo had killed themselves.\n\nHe also openly supported Serbian leader Milosevic.\n\nAfter the ceremony, Bosnian Croat President Zeljko Komsic said the Srebrenica genocide was awarded on the occasion.\n\nVucic, however, congratulated Handke and also invited him to visit Serbia.\n\n- 29th anniversary\n\nEuropean Union foreign policy chief Josep Borrell said Wednesday that they must honor the memory of the over 8,300 boys and men who were systematically murdered in the hills around Srebrenica in Bosnia and Herzegovina, stressing the need to bring all perpetrators of the 1995 genocide to justice.\n\n\"Healing the wounds of the past requires acknowledging and teaching the historical facts, honoring and remembering the victims, identifying those still missing, and bringing all perpetrators to justice. This is key to confronting the roots of hatred that led to the genocide.\"\n\nThere is no place for those who deny genocide, try to rewrite history, and glorify war criminals, Borrell warned, stressing that they need to build together bridges to reconciliation.\n\nThe International Srebrenica Motorcycle Marathon is being held for the 13th time this year under the theme \"Not to be Forgotten, Not to Be Repeated.\"\n\nMotorcyclists passed through Sarajevo's main streets on Wednesday, as they have done in the past, and residents expressed their enthusiasm for their participation in honoring those massacred in 1995.\n\nThe motorcyclists paid their respects and left flowers in front of the Monument to the Murdered Children before continuing to the Potocari Memorial Cemetery.\n\nEvery year on July 11, newly identified victims of the genocide are buried in the memorial cemetery in Potocari.\n\nThe youngest victim to be buried this year is Beriz Mujic, 17, born in 1978 in Zvornik.\n\nIn May 2023, his remains were found 28 years after his killing and exhumed.\n\nHe was killed in July 1995 in the Suceska area near Bratunac.\n\nMujic will be buried next to his brother Hazim, whose remains were laid to rest in 2013.\n\nThe body of their father, Omer Mujic, has yet to be found.\n\nThe oldest victim who will be buried on Thursday is Hamed Salic, born in 1927. He was 68 years old when he went missing in the summer of 1995 in the town of Zepa. His remains were exhumed in May 2014 and recently identified.\n\nThousands of people from various countries will attend the funerals and burials. Following this year's funeral, the cemetery's total number of burials will reach 6,765.", "source": {"uri": "yenisafak.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "Yeni \u015eafak"}, "authors": [{"uri": Thousands gather in the eastern Bosnian town of Srebrenica to commemorate the 29th anniversary on Monday of Europe's only acknowledged genocide since World War II. (AP [...]\n\nSREBRENICA, Bosnia-Herzegovina (AP) -- Thousands of people from Bosnia and abroad gathered in Srebrenica on Thursday for the annual ritual of commemorating the 1995 genocide which Serb officials continue to deny, fueling ethnic tensions and deep divisions within the war-ravaged state.\n\nTwenty-nine years after they were murdered in Europe's only acknowledged genocide since the Holocaust, the bodies of 13 men and one teenage boy were laid to rest Thursday at a vast and ever-expanding memorial cemetery just outside Srebrenica, in eastern Bosnia. They join more than 6,600 massacre victims already reburied there.\n\nMore than 8,000 Bosniak Muslims were estimated to have been killed in the shooting spree by the Bosnian Serb army and police over several days in July 1995.\n\nRelatives of the victims can bury only partial remains of their loved ones as they are typically found scattered over several different mass graves, sometimes miles (kilometers) apart.\n\nThe Srebrenica killings were the bloody crescendo of Bosnia's 1992-95 war, which came after the breakup of Yugoslavia unleashed nationalist passions and territorial ambitions that set Bosnian Serbs against the country's two other main ethnic populations -- Croats and Bosniaks, who are mostly Muslim.\n\nThe commemoration Thursday came only weeks after the United Nations General Assembly voted to designate July 11 annually as an international day of reflection and commemoration of the 1995 Srebrenica genocide. Serbia and Bosnian Serbs strongly opposed its adoption, wrongly claiming it portrays all Serbs as \"genocidal people.\"\n\nSerb leaders insist the massacre is not genocide, but a \"terrible crime.\" They have also downplayed the number of those killed.\n\n\"The genocide in Srebrenica did not happen, and if it did, there would be no need to constantly impose this topic,\" Bosnian Serb separatist President Milorad Dodik has repeatedly said.\n\nPresident of the Board of Directors of the Srebrenica Memorial Center, Hamdija Fejzic, said that the genocide denial must stop.\n\n\"For a full 29 years, the policy of covering up and denying the genocide was carried out by those forces who designed and planned the genocide, and who for years provided shelter to those suspected and accused of the most serious war crimes,\" he told the gathering on Thursday.\n\nIn an op-ed piece in Bosnian media, European Union High Representative Josep Borrell said \"Srebrenica remains a deep scar in the history of Europe.\"\n\n\"The failure to prevent this genocide is a burden we continue to bear,\" he wrote. \"Both the International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia and the International Court of Justice have indisputably determined that this crime is genocide.\"\n\n\"We promised that we would never forget -- neither the victims, nor the lasting pain of their families and loved ones,\" he added. \"Their memory drives us to work every day to ensure that history does not repeat itself, in a world where peace seems increasingly fragile.\"\n\nOn July 11, 1995, Bosnian Serbs overran a U.N.-protected safe area in Srebrenica. They separated more than 8,000 Bosniak men and boys from their wives, mothers and sisters and slaughtered them. Those who tried to escape were chased through the woods and over the mountains around the ill-fated town.\n\nThe perpetrators then dumped their victims' bodies into hastily made mass graves, which they later dug up with bulldozers, scattering the remains among other burial sites to hide the evidence of their war crimes.\n\nThe Bosnian Serb wartime political leader Radovan Karadzic and his military commander Ratko Mladic were both convicted of genocide in Srebrenica by a special U.N. war crimes tribunal in The Hague. In all, the tribunal and courts in the Balkans have sentenced close to 50 Bosnian Serb wartime officials to more than 700 years in prison for the Srebrenica killings.\n\nHowever, most Serbian and Bosnian Serb officials still celebrate Karadzic and Mladic as national heroes. They continue to downplay or even deny the Srebrenica killings and offend the massacre victims and survivors.\n\n-- --\n\nAssociated Press Writer Dusan Stojanovic contributed to this story from The remainder of the Bosnian Muslim population present in Srebrenica - approximately 25,000 women, children and elderly - were forcibly transferred out of the enclave.\n\nThis was the largest massacre in Europe since the Holocaust.\n\nTo date, only a few events have been determined by competent judicial bodies to constitute genocide. The International Court of Justice (ICJ) and the International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia (ICTY) recognized the massacre of Bosnian Muslims in Srebrenica by the army of Republika Srpska as an act of genocide.\n\nRemembering the victims\n\nThe genocide left deep emotional scars on the survivors, families of victims, and the Bosnian and Herzegovinian society in general, creating enduring obstacles to reconciliation among the country's different ethnic groups.\n\n2025 will mark the thirtieth anniversary of the genocide in Srebrenica, in which at least 8,372 lives were lost, thousands were displaced and families and communities were devastated.\n\nUnited Nations Special Adviser on the Prevention of Genocide, Alice Wairimu Nderitu has expressed her concern over continuous incidents of revisionism concerning atrocity crimes perpetrated during the 1992-1995 conflict, including unabated denial of the Srebrenica genocide and glorification of convicted war criminals.\n\nA day of reflection and commemoration\n\nIn May 2024, The UN General Assembly, in a resolution sponsored by Germany and Rwanda, designated 11 July as the International Day of Reflection and Commemoration of the 1995 Genocide in Srebrenica.\n\nThe Assembly also asked the Secretary-General to establish an outreach programme on the Srebrenica genocide in preparation for the 30th anniversary.\n\nIt further condemned any denial of the Srebrenica genocide as a historical event and called on Member States to preserve the established facts, including through their educational systems, towards preventing denial and distortion, and any occurrence of genocide in the future.\n\nThe inaugural observance is being marked with a high-level commemorative event, organized by the They ended up like this only because they had a (Muslim) name,\" said Mevlida Hasanovic as she prayed at the tomb of her cousin, who was 18 when he was killed.\n\nMs Hasanovic lost a dozen male relatives in the massacre including her father and husband, whose grave is next to her cousin's.\n\nHis remains were buried twice as they were found in two different mass graves.\n\nThe 54-year-old woman is still waiting for \"at least one bone\" of a brother to be found so she can bury him.\n\n\"Their souls know that we are here next to them. When I get here, I feel as if we just parted ways in Srebrenica,\" she said.\n\nThe adoption of the UN General Assembly resolution to declare an International Day of Reflection and Commemoration of the genocide was fiercely opposed by Serbia and Bosnian Serbs, who continue to play down the crime.\n\nBosnian Serb leader Milorad Dodik has repeatedly denied a genocide occurred and says his administration will not recognise the resolution.\n\nBut Mr Dodik expressed sympathy to the families of the victims today.\n\n\"Regardless of our differences, we must show respect for the pain and suffering that has befallen many people of all nations and religions in Bosnia and Herzegovina,\" Mr Dodik said on X.\n\nA UN court sentenced Bosnian Serb wartime political leader Radovan Karadzic and his army chief Mladic to life in prison for war crimes including the Srebrenica genocide.\n\nBosnia's 1992-1995 war between its Croats, Muslims and Serbs claimed approximately 100,000 lives.\n\nNearly three decades after the war ended, the Balkan nation remains deeply divided along ethnic lines.\n\nVictims of the genocide continue to be laid to rest\n\nThe remains of 14 more victims of the bloodshed, including a 17-year-old boy, will be buried at a memorial cemetery in Potocari, just outside Srebrenica.\n\nBeriz Mujic, whose remains were found in the Srebrenica region last year, will be laid to rest next to his brother Hazim.\n\nThe remains of 6,988 Srebrenica victims have been buried, most of them under white tombstones in Potocari.\n\nThe remains were found in 87 mass graves, and a spokeswoman for Bosnia's institute for missing persons said that they are still looking for around 1,000 people.\n\nTo cover up the crime, Bosnian Serb forces moved the bodies of the victims to so-called secondary mass graves.\n\nKada Sikovic, accompanied by her two daughters and son, stood by the coffin of her husband, Musan, with tears rolling down her face.\n\nParts of his chin bone were recovered in 2010 but she had resisted holding a burial ceremony until more remains were found last year.\n\n\"Thank God we found some of his bones,\" she said.\n\nShe remembered the painful moment when the family split in Srebrenica in 1995.\n\n\"He cried, kissed the girl (daughter), took the little one (five-year-old) son in his arms and said: 'See you'.\"\n\nYesterday, the European Union, which Bosnia aspires to join, called the atrocity \"one of the darkest moments in modern European history\".\n\n\"There is no place amongst us for those who deny genocide, attempt to rewrite history, and glorify war criminals,\" EU foreign policy chief Josep Borrell and the bloc's enlargement commissioner Oliver Varhelyi said in a joint statement.\n\nAdditional reporting AFP", "source": {"uri": {"uri": "2024-07-418583217", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-11", "time": "11:45:49", "dateTime": "2024-07-11T11:45:49Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-11T10:55:49Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7882353067398071, "url": "https://www.beaumontenterprise.com/news/world/article/thousands-mark-1995-srebrenica-genocide-which-is-19566892.php", "title": "Thousands mark 1995 Srebrenica genocide which is denied by Serbs, fueling ethnic tensions in Bosnia", "body": "SREBRENICA, Bosnia-Herzegovina (AP) -- Thousands of people from Bosnia and abroad gathered in Srebrenica on Thursday for the annual ritual of commemorating the 1995 genocide which Serb officials continue to deny, fueling ethnic tensions and deep divisions within the war-ravaged state.\n\nTwenty-nine years after they were murdered in Europe's only acknowledged genocide since the Holocaust, the bodies of 13 men and one teenage boy were laid to rest Thursday at a vast and ever-expanding memorial cemetery just outside Srebrenica, in eastern Bosnia. They join more than 6,600 massacre victims already reburied there.\n\nMore than 8,000 Bosniak Muslims were estimated to have been killed in the shooting spree by the Bosnian Serb army and police over several days in July 1995.\n\nRelatives of the victims can bury only partial remains of their loved ones as they are typically found scattered over several different mass graves, sometimes miles (kilometers) apart.\n\nThe Srebrenica killings were the bloody crescendo of Bosnia's 1992-95 war, which came after the breakup of Yugoslavia unleashed nationalist passions and territorial ambitions that set Bosnian Serbs against the country's two other main ethnic populations -- Croats and Bosniaks, who are mostly Muslim.\n\nThe commemoration Thursday came only weeks after the United Nations General Assembly voted to designate July 11 annually as an international day of reflection and commemoration of the 1995 Srebrenica genocide. Serbia and Bosnian Serbs strongly opposed its adoption, wrongly claiming it portrays all Serbs as \"genocidal people.\"\n\nSerb leaders insist the massacre is not genocide, but a \"terrible crime.\" They have also downplayed the number of those killed.\n\n\"The genocide in Srebrenica did not happen, and if it did, there would be no need to constantly impose this topic,\" Bosnian Serb separatist President Milorad Dodik has repeatedly said.\n\nPresident of the Board of Directors of the Srebrenica Memorial Center, Hamdija Fejzic, said that the genocide denial must stop.\n\n\"For a full 29 years, the policy of covering up and denying the genocide was carried out by those forces who designed and planned the genocide, and who for years provided shelter to those suspected and accused of the most serious war crimes,\" he told the gathering on Thursday.\n\nIn an op-ed piece in Bosnian media, European Union High Representative Josep Borrell said \"Srebrenica remains a deep scar in the history of Europe.\"\n\n\"The failure to prevent this genocide is a burden we continue to bear,\" he wrote. \"Both the International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia and the International Court of Justice have indisputably determined that this crime is genocide.\"\n\n\"We promised that we would never forget -- neither the victims, nor the lasting pain of their families and loved ones,\" he added. \"Their memory drives us to work every day to ensure that history does not repeat itself, in a world where peace seems increasingly fragile.\"\n\nOn July 11, 1995, Bosnian Serbs overran a U.N.-protected safe area in Srebrenica. They separated more than 8,000 Bosniak men and boys from their wives, mothers and sisters and slaughtered them. Those who tried to escape were chased through the woods and over the mountains around the ill-fated town.\n\nThe perpetrators then dumped their victims' bodies into hastily made mass graves, which they later dug up with bulldozers, scattering the remains among other burial sites to hide the evidence of their war crimes.\n\nThe Bosnian Serb wartime political leader Radovan Karadzic and his military commander Ratko Mladic were both convicted of genocide in Srebrenica by a special U.N. war crimes tribunal in The Hague. In all, the tribunal and courts in the Balkans have sentenced close to 50 Bosnian Serb wartime officials to more than 700 years in prison for the Srebrenica killings.\n\nHowever, most Serbian and Bosnian Serb officials still celebrate Karadzic and Mladic as national heroes. They continue to downplay or even deny the Srebrenica killings and offend the massacre victims and survivors.\n\n-- --\n\nAssociated Press Writer Dusan Stojanovic contributed to this story from {"uri": "8220021308", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-11", "time": "08:03:13", "dateTime": "2024-07-11T08:03:13Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-11T08:02:43Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7843137383460999, "url": "https://www.aa.com.tr/en/europe/bosnia-marks-29th-anniversary-of-srebrenica-genocide/3271966", "title": "Bosnia marks 29th anniversary of Srebrenica genocide", "body": "Memorial Ceremony ahead of 29th Srebrenica Genocide Anniversary\n\nBosnia and Herzegovina marked the 29th anniversary of the Srebrenica genocide Thursday in the wake of several developments since the killing of more than 8,000 civilians in July 1995, including the sentencing of 45 of those responsible for the atrocity to nearly 700 years in prison.\n\nOn Dec. 21, 1991, Bosnian Serbs proclaimed their own republic after voting against independence from Yugoslavia in a referendum.\n\nOn Jan. 9, 1992, they proclaimed the Republic of the Serbian People in Bosnia-Herzegovina but did not officially declare independence.\n\nBosnia and Herzegovina formally declared independence following a referendum held on Feb. 29 and March 1, 1992, which sparked a three-year war.\n\nThe war lasted until Dec. 14, 1995, and more than 100,000 people were killed and 2 million had to migrate.\n\nThe UN Security Council in the spring of 1993 declared Srebrenica a \"safe area.\" But Serb troops led by Gen. Ratko Mladic - who was later found guilty of war crimes, crimes against humanity and genocide - overran the UN zone.\n\nThe fate of approximately 7,000 people who disappeared during the war is still unknown.\n\nIn a case heard at the International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia (ICTY) in The Hague, the Netherlands, Serbian commander Mladic was sentenced to life imprisonment for many crimes, including genocide. The sentence was approved at an appeal hearing on June 8, 2021.\n\nRadovan Karadzic, the leader of the Bosnian Serbs during the Bosnian War, was sentenced to 40 years in prison for many crimes, including the Srebrenica Genocide, and then to life imprisonment in an appeal case.\n\nIn the Srebrenica cases heard at the ICTY, former Serbian officials Ljubisa Beara and Vujadin Popovic were also sentenced to life imprisonment.\n\nIn its decision in 2007, the International Court of Justice in The Hague described what happened in Srebrenica and its surroundings as a \"genocide,\" based on evidence from the ICTY.\n\nFormer Serbian President Slobodan Milosevic died in prison while his trial was ongoing.\n\nIn the Srebrenica cases heard at the ICTY, Drago Nikolic was sentenced to 35 years in prison, Radislav Krstic to 35 years, Radivoje Miletic to 19 years, Ljubomir Borovcanin to 17 years, Vidoje Blagojevic to 15 years, Vinko Pandurevic to 13 years and Milan Gvero to five years.\n\nIn a case at the Court of Bosnia and Herzegovina, Milorad Trbic was found guilty of genocide and was sentenced to 30 years in prison for his part in the killing of nearly 1,000 Bosnian civilians in July 1995.\n\nTo date, 45 Serbs have been sentenced to a total of 699 years in prison in cases heard in different courts.\n\nMost of the Bosnian male civilians who took shelter in a battery factory used as a base by Dutch UN soldiers were killed by Serbs there.\n\nDespite the passing of years, the role of Dutch UN soldiers in the genocide continued to be debated.\n\nIn images taken after the occupation of Srebrenica, Dutch commander Thom Karremans was seen meeting with Mladic on July 11, 1995. It was noted that Mladic bought Karremans a drink at the end of the footage and the two toasted together.\n\nWhile Karremans was never tried for what happened, the Dutch state was found \"partially\" guilty of the genocide in Srebrenica.\n\nThe Dutch government in 2022 apologized to Bosniak families who lost their relatives in the genocide.\n\nFormer Defense Minister Kajsa Ollongren offered the apology at the 27th commemoration of the genocide at the cemetery in the village of Potocari in Bosnia and Herzegovina.\n\n''Despite everything, Srebrenica was crushed...The Netherlands is also a part of this failure. For this reason, we offer you our deepest apologies,'' said Ollongren.\n\nShe said international institutions had promised to protect innocent people.\n\n\"The international community failed to protect the people of Srebrenica. As part of this community, the Dutch government shares political responsibility for the situation in which this failure could happen...We cannot take away the suffering. But what we can do is look history straight in the eye,\" she added.\n\nIn a lawsuit filed in 2007 by relatives of the victims against the Dutch government, The Hague District Court found The Netherlands guilty of handing over 300 Bosniak civilians to the Serbs who had taken refuge with Dutch soldiers and the United Nations during the occupation of Srebrenica.\n\nThe UN in late May this year passed a resolution to designate July 11 as the \"International Day of Reflection and Commemoration of the 1995 Genocide in Srebrenica\" with overwhelming support from the General Assembly.\n\nThe resolution was spearheaded by Germany, with co-sponsorship from more than 40 countries.\n\nIt passed with 84 nations voting in favor and 19 against. A total of 68 countries abstained.\n\nCondemning the denial of the Srebrenica genocide, the resolution denounced the glorification of crimes against humanity, genocide and war criminals.\n\nHighlighting the importance of ongoing efforts for the identification of victims and the retrieval of bodies, the resolution emphasizes the need for all perpetrators to be brought to justice.\n\nSerbian President Aleksandar Vucic argued before the vote that the resolution was \"highly politicized.\"\n\nHe said individuals responsible for the genocide had been punished and that the resolution would neither contribute to the stability and unity of Bosnia and Herzegovina nor the region, but would increase divisions.\n\nAccusing Germany of threatening countries that did not support the resolution, Vucic said: \"Is that European values, democratic values?\"\n\nWhile not legally binding, General Assembly resolutions carry political weight and send a strong message to the international community.\n\nT\u00fcrkiye has officially declared July 11 as the \"International Day of Reflection and Remembrance of the Srebrenica Genocide,\" according to a presidential decree published in the Official Gazette on Wednesday.\n\nMentioning the UN's adoption of the resolution, the decree noted that the resolution unequivocally condemns actions that glorify those convicted by international courts of war crimes, crimes against humanity and genocide, including those responsible for the Srebrenica genocide in Bosnia and Herzegovina.\n\n\"July 11, accepted as the 'International Day of Reflection and Remembrance of the Srebrenica Genocide,' will be commemorated in our country to share the pain, condemn genocide and crimes against humanity, and raise global awareness through special remembrance events, educational activities and public awareness initiatives in honor of the victims of the Srebrenica genocide,\" it added.\n\nKosovo is another country that decided Wednesday to declare July 11 Srebrenica genocide remembrance day to honor the memory of the victims.\n\n''As one of the first countries to implement the UN resolution on the Srebrenica genocide, the Republic of Kosovo has just decided, as the first topic of our government meeting today, that July 11 will be designated as the official Commemoration Day for Srebrenica,'' said Foreign Minister Donika Gervalla-Schwarz.\n\nIn 2017, then-Serbian President Tomislav Nikolic apologized for all \"crimes\" committed by Serbs during the break-up of Yugoslavia, including Srebrenica.\n\nBut he refused to call the killing of thousands of Bosnian Muslims an act of genocide.\n\nSerbia has never accepted the killings as genocide.\n\nNikolic said he was kneeling and seeking forgiveness for Srebrenica.\n\nIn 2015, then-Prime Minister Aleksandar Vucic attended the commemoration ceremony on July 11 and paid respect to the victims. However, he quickly left the ceremony after being attacked by a stone-throwing mob.\n\nVucic has termed the incident involving him getting chased out from the mass burial ceremony during the 20th anniversary of the Srebrenica genocide in Bosnia-Herzegovina as politically motivated.\n\nHe was forced to flee with his bodyguards on July 11, 2015 under a hail of stones thrown by mourners at a funeral prayer and burial service for 136 Srebrenica victims whose remains were recently discovered.\n\nPeople from the Bosnian village of Potocari - the scene of the genocide of Bosnian Muslim men and boys in 1995 - shouted \"Justice!\" and \"Vucic leave!\" as the Serbian premier was immediately forced to leave the cemetery.\n\n\"This was an organized attack laced with political messages. I am happy (to know) that it was not organized by the victims' families. I heard some Muslims from among the crowd say 'he is not guilty,'\" Vucic said after an emergency government meeting upon his return to the Serbian capital Belgrade.\n\nHe said he was given a warm welcome by the victims' families and the Bosniak mayor of Srebrenica, Camil Durakovic, upon his arrival at the memorial and cemetery complex, adding he refused to hide, despite hearing slogans demanding that he be \"shot.\"\n\n\"I was physically attacked as I was proceeding to the designated seating area, and my glasses fell off my face and broke,\" Vucic said. \"I am sorry that such an incident occurred and some people did not respond to our intention of building a friendship between Bosnians and Serbs.\"\n\nHe added that he would continue to extend his hand to the Bosnian people, the majority of whom, he said, condemned the attack on him.\n\n\"I am the one who extends his hand to you and wants to have peace with you. This is our policy,\" he said.\n\nVucic also urged the Serbian people \"to not raise their hands to anyone, thinking they can do anything they want,\" as \"we have to live together with the Bosniaks in the future too.\"\n\nCouncil of Europe: Serbia must recognize 1995 genocide\n\nA Council of Europe body in 2017 called on Serbia to officially recognize the 1995 Srebrenica massacre as a genocide and to punish those responsible.\n\nThe European Commission Against Racism and Intolerance (ECRI) published its annual report on Serbia and also said that hate speech and hate crimes were on the increase in the Balkan state.\n\nIt said Belgrade should \"actively implement\" a strategy to punish those guilty of war crimes.\n\nSrebrenica genocide denier awarded Nobel medal\n\nIn 2019, the Swedish Academy picked a 77-year-old Austrian author, Peter Handke, for the Nobel Prize in literature, despite his denial of the Srebrenica genocide.\n\nThe academy's choice was met with backlash worldwide.\n\nHandke claimed that Muslim Bosniaks in Sarajevo had killed themselves.\n\nHe also openly supported Serbian leader Milosevic.\n\nSeveral countries, including T\u00fcrkiye, boycotted the award ceremony and the Turkish, Albanian, Kosovar and Croatian envoys to Sweden also did not attend.\n\nAfter the ceremony, Bosnian Croat President Zeljko Komsic said the Srebrenica genocide was awarded on the occasion.\n\nVucic, however, congratulated Handke and also invited him to visit Serbia.\n\n29th anniversary\n\nEuropean Union foreign policy chief Josep Borrell said Wednesday that they must honor the memory of the over 8,300 boys and men who were systematically murdered in the hills around Srebrenica in Bosnia and Herzegovina, stressing the need to bring all perpetrators of the 1995 genocide to justice.\n\nBorrell issued a statement the day before the 29th anniversary of the Srebrenica genocide, urging leaders to reject divisive rhetoric and act with truth, justice and dialogue.\n\n\"Healing the wounds of the past requires acknowledging and teaching the historical facts, honoring and remembering the victims, identifying those still missing, and bringing all perpetrators to justice. This is key to confronting the roots of hatred that led to the genocide.\"\n\nThere is no place for those who deny genocide, try to rewrite history, and glorify war criminals, Borrell warned, stressing that they need to build together bridges to reconciliation.\n\nMeanwhile, hundreds of motorcyclists from various countries gathered in the Bosnian capital Sarajevo to ride in a convoy to the Potocari Memorial Cemetery in Srebrenica in memory of the genocide victims.\n\nThe International Srebrenica Motorcycle Marathon is being held for the 13th time this year under the theme \"Not to be Forgotten, Not to Be Repeated.\"\n\nMotorcyclists passed through Sarajevo's main streets on Wednesday, as they have done in the past, and residents expressed their enthusiasm for their participation in honoring those massacred in 1995.\n\nThe motorcyclists paid their respects and left flowers in front of the Monument to the Murdered Children before continuing to the Potocari Memorial Cemetery.\n\nOn Tuesday, Bosnia and Herzegovina sent the remains of 14 more Srebrenica genocide victims to Potocari village, three days before their burial on the 29th anniversary of the 1995 genocide.\n\nEvery year on July 11, newly identified victims of the genocide are buried in the memorial cemetery in Potocari.\n\nThe youngest victim to be buried this year is Beriz Mujic, 17, born in 1978 in Zvornik.\n\nIn May 2023, his remains were found 28 years after his killing and exhumed.\n\nHe was killed in July 1995 in the Suceska area near Bratunac.\n\nMujic will be buried next to his brother Hazim, whose remains were laid to rest in 2013.\n\nThe body of their father, Omer Mujic, has yet to be found.\n\nThe oldest victim who will be buried on Thursday is Hamed Salic, born in 1927. He was 68 years old when he went missing in the summer of 1995 in the town of Zepa. His remains were exhumed in May 2014 and recently identified.\n\nThousands of people from various countries will attend the funerals and burials. Following this year's funeral, the cemetery's total number of burials will reach 6,765.", "source": {"uri": "aa.com.tr", "dataType": "news", "title": "Anadolu Ajans\u0131"}, "authors": [], "concepts": {"uri": "2024-07-418533540", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-11", "time": "11:02:23", "dateTime": "2024-07-11T11:02:23Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-11T06:53:00Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7843137383460999, "url": "https://www.usnews.com/news/world/articles/2024-07-11/thousands-mark-1995-srebrenica-genocide-which-is-denied-by-serbs-fueling-ethnic-tensions-in-bosnia", "title": "Thousands Mark 1995 Srebrenica Genocide Which Is Denied by Serbs, Fueling Ethnic Tensions in Bosnia", "body": "SREBRENICA, Bosnia-Herzegovina (AP) -- Thousands of people from Bosnia and abroad gathered in Srebrenica on Thursday for the annual ritual of commemorating the 1995 genocide which Serb officials continue to deny, fueling ethnic tensions and deep divisions within the war-ravaged state.\n\nTwenty-nine years after they were murdered in Europe's only acknowledged genocide since the Holocaust, the bodies of 13 men and one teenage boy were laid to rest Thursday at a vast and ever-expanding memorial cemetery just outside Srebrenica, in eastern Bosnia. They join more than 6,600 massacre victims already reburied there.\n\nMore than 8,000 Bosniak Muslims were estimated to have been killed in the shooting spree by the Bosnian Serb army and police over several days in July 1995.\n\nRelatives of the victims can bury only partial remains of their loved ones as they are typically found scattered over several different mass graves, sometimes miles (kilometers) apart.\n\nThe Srebrenica killings were the bloody crescendo of Bosnia's 1992-95 war, which came after the breakup of Yugoslavia unleashed nationalist passions and territorial ambitions that set Bosnian Serbs against the country's two other main ethnic populations -- Croats and Bosniaks, who are mostly Muslim.\n\nThe commemoration Thursday came only weeks after the United Nations General Assembly voted to designate July 11 annually as an international day of reflection and commemoration of the 1995 Srebrenica genocide. Serbia and Bosnian Serbs strongly opposed its adoption, wrongly claiming it portrays all Serbs as \"genocidal people.\"\n\nSerb leaders insist the massacre is not genocide, but a \"terrible crime.\" They have also downplayed the number of those killed.\n\n\"The genocide in Srebrenica did not happen, and if it did, there would be no need to constantly impose this topic,\" Bosnian Serb separatist President Milorad Dodik has repeatedly said.\n\nPresident of the Board of Directors of the Srebrenica Memorial Center, Hamdija Fejzic, said that the genocide denial must stop.\n\n\"For a full 29 years, the policy of covering up and denying the genocide was carried out by those forces who designed and planned the genocide, and who for years provided shelter to those suspected and accused of the most serious war crimes,\" he told the gathering on Thursday.\n\nIn an op-ed piece in Bosnian media, European Union High Representative Josep Borrell said \"Srebrenica remains a deep scar in the history of Europe.\"\n\n\"The failure to prevent this genocide is a burden we continue to bear,\" he wrote. \"Both the International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia and the International Court of Justice have indisputably determined that this crime is genocide.\"\n\n\"We promised that we would never forget -- neither the victims, nor the lasting pain of their families and loved ones,\" he added. \"Their memory drives us to work every day to ensure that history does not repeat itself, in a world where peace seems increasingly fragile.\"\n\nOn July 11, 1995, Bosnian Serbs overran a U.N.-protected safe area in Srebrenica. They separated more than 8,000 Bosniak men and boys from their wives, mothers and sisters and slaughtered them. Those who tried to escape were chased through the woods and over the mountains around the ill-fated town.\n\nThe perpetrators then dumped their victims' bodies into hastily made mass graves, which they later dug up with bulldozers, scattering the remains among other burial sites to hide the evidence of their war crimes.\n\nThe Bosnian Serb wartime political leader Radovan Karadzic and his military commander Ratko Mladic were both convicted of genocide in Srebrenica by a special U.N. war crimes tribunal in The Hague. In all, the tribunal and courts in the Balkans have sentenced close to 50 Bosnian Serb wartime officials to more than 700 years in prison for the Srebrenica killings.\n\nHowever, most Serbian and Bosnian Serb officials still celebrate Karadzic and Mladic as national heroes. They continue to downplay or even deny the Srebrenica killings and offend the massacre victims and survivors.\n\n-- --\n\nAssociated Press Writer Dusan Stojanovic contributed to this story from Belgrade, Serbia.\n\nCopyright 2024 The Associated Press. They ended up like this only because they had a different (Muslim) name,\" said Mevlida Hasanovic as she prayed at the tomb of her cousin, who was 18 when he was killed.\n\nHasanovic lost a dozen male relatives in the massacre including her father and husband, whose grave is next to her cousin's.\n\nHis remains were buried on two occasions since they were found in two different mass graves.\n\nThe 54-year-old woman is still looking for the remains of a brother to be found, \"at least one bone\", to bury him, she told AFP.\n\n\"Their souls know that we are here next to them. When I get here, I feel as if we just parted ways in Srebrenica.\"\n\nIn May, the United Nations General Assembly adopted a resolution declaring July 11 the \"International Day of Reflection and Commemoration of the 1995 Genocide in Srebrenica\".\n\nThe resolution was fiercly opposed by Serbia and Bosnian Serbs, who continue to play down the crime.\n\nBosnian Serb leader Milorad Dodik has repeatedly denied a genocide occurred, and says his administration would not recognise the resolution.\n\nA UN court sentenced Bosnian Serb wartime political leader Radovan Karadzic and his army chief Ratko Mladic to life in prison for war crimes including the Srebrenica genocide.\n\nBosnia's 1992-1995 war between its Croats, Muslims and Serbs claimed approximately 100,000 lives.\n\nNearly three decades after the war ended, the Balkan nation remains deeply divided along ethnic lines.\n\nNew burial\n\nOn Thursday, the remains of 14 more victims of the bloodshed, including a 17-year-old boy, will be buried at a memorial cemetery in Potocari, just outside Srebrenica.\n\nBeriz Mujic, whose remains were found in the Srebrenica region last year, will be laid to rest next to his brother Hazim.\n\nSo far, the remains, often incomplete, of 6,988 Srebrenica victims have been buried, the overwhelming majority of them under white tombstones in Potocari.\n\nThe remains were found in 87 mass graves, and a spokeswoman for Bosnia's institute for missing persons told AFP that they are still looking for around 1,000 people.\n\nTo cover up the crime, Bosnian Serb forces moved the bodies of the victims to so-called secondary mass graves.\n\nOn Wednesday, the European Union, which Bosnia aspires to join, called the atrocity \"one of the darkest moments in modern European history\".\n\n\"There is no place amongst us for those who deny genocide, attempt to rewrite history, and glorify war criminals,\" EU foreign policy chief Josep Borrell and EU enlargement commissioner Oliver Varhelyi said in a joint statement.\n\nThe annual commemoration ceremonies started on Monday with a 100-kilometre (62-mile) march towards Srebrenica.\n\nSeveral thousand people joined the march {"uri": "2024-07-418691907", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-11", "time": "13:16:04", "dateTime": "2024-07-11T13:16:04Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-11T13:15:35Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7686274647712708, "url": "http://english.ahram.org.eg/NewsContent/2/9/527054/World/International/Thousands-mark--Srebrenica-genocide-which-is-denie.aspx", "title": "Thousands mark 1995 Srebrenica genocide which is denied by Serbs, fueling ethnic tensions in Bosnia", "body": "Twenty-nine years after they were murdered in Europe's only acknowledged genocide since the Holocaust, the bodies of 13 men and one teenage boy were laid to rest Thursday at a vast and ever-expanding memorial cemetery just outside Srebrenica, in eastern Bosnia. They join more than 6,600 massacre victims already reburied there.\n\nMore than 8,000 Bosniak Muslims were estimated to have been killed in the shooting spree by the Bosnian Serb army and police over several days in July 1995.\n\nRelatives of the victims can bury only partial remains of their loved ones as they are typically found scattered over several different mass graves, sometimes miles (kilometres) apart.\n\nThe Srebrenica killings were the bloody crescendo of Bosnia's 1992-95 war, which came after the breakup of Yugoslavia unleashed nationalist passions and territorial ambitions that set Bosnian Serbs against the country's two other main ethnic populations -- Croats and Bosniaks, who are mostly Muslim.\n\nThe commemoration Thursday came only weeks after the United Nations General Assembly voted to designate July 11 annually as an international day of reflection and commemoration of the 1995 Srebrenica genocide. Serbia and Bosnian Serbs strongly opposed its adoption, wrongly claiming it portrays all Serbs as \"genocidal people.\"\n\nSerb leaders insist the massacre is not genocide, but a \"terrible crime.\" They have also downplayed the number of those killed.\n\n\"The genocide in Srebrenica did not happen, and if it did, there would be no need to constantly impose this topic,\" Bosnian Serb separatist President Milorad Dodik has repeatedly said.\n\nPresident of the Board of Directors of the Srebrenica Memorial Center, Hamdija Fejzic, said that the genocide denial must stop.\n\n\"For a full 29 years, the policy of covering up and denying the genocide was carried out by those forces who designed and planned the genocide, and who for years provided shelter to those suspected and accused of the most serious war crimes,\" he told the gathering on Thursday.\n\nIn an op-ed piece in Bosnian media, European Union High Representative Josep Borrell said \"Srebrenica remains a deep scar in the history of Europe.\"\n\n\"The failure to prevent this genocide is a burden we continue to bear,\" he wrote. \"Both the International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia and the International Court of Justice have indisputably determined that this crime is genocide.\"\n\n\"We promised that we would never forget -- neither the victims nor the lasting pain of their families and loved ones,\" he added. \"Their memory drives us to work every day to ensure that history does not repeat itself, in a world where peace seems increasingly fragile.\"\n\nOn July 11, 1995, Bosnian Serbs overran a U.N.-protected safe area in Srebrenica. They separated more than 8,000 Bosniak men and boys from their wives, mothers and sisters and slaughtered them. Those who tried to escape were chased through the woods and over the mountains around the ill-fated town.\n\nThe perpetrators then dumped their victims' bodies into hastily made mass graves, which they later dug up with bulldozers, scattering the remains among other burial sites to hide the evidence of their war crimes.\n\nThe Bosnian Serb wartime political leader Radovan Karadzic and his military commander Ratko Mladic were both convicted of genocide in Srebrenica by a special U.N. war crimes tribunal in The Hague. In all, the tribunal and courts in the Balkans have sentenced close to 50 Bosnian Serb wartime officials to more than 700 years in prison for the Srebrenica killings.\n\nHowever, most Serbian and Bosnian Serb officials still celebrate Karadzic and Mladic as national heroes. He was 68 when he went missing in the summer of 1995 in the town of Zepa. His remains were exhumed in May 2014 and recently identified.\n\nThousands of people from various countries will attend the funerals and burials. Following this year's funeral, the number of victims buried at the cemetery will reach 6,765.\n\nSrebrenica genocide\n\nIn the spring of 1993, the UN Security Council declared the city of Srebrenica a \"safe area.\" However, Serb troops led by Gen. Ratko Mladic, who was later found guilty of war crimes, crimes against humanity, and genocide, overran the zone.\n\nDutch troops responsible for safeguarding people in the UN zone failed to act when Serb forces occupied it on July 11, killing 2,000 men and boys in a single day.\n\nApproximately 15,000 Bosniaks fled to the surrounding mountains, but Serb troops hunted them down, killing an additional 6,000 people.\n\nSerb forces allowed women and children to reach Bosnian-controlled regions but massacred at least 8,372 Bosnian men in forests, factories, and warehouses. The murdered Bosnians were buried in mass graves, with bodies discovered in 570 different locations across the country, including 77 mass graves.\n\nIn 2007, the International Court of Justice in The Hague ruled that genocide had been committed in Srebrenica.\n\nEfforts to locate the missing victims of the genocide have continued, with identified remains buried at the Potocari Memorial Cemetery.\n\nOn June 8, 2021, UN tribunal judges upheld a life sentence for Mladic for genocide, persecution, crimes against humanity, extermination, and other war crimes committed in Bosnia and One participant passed away during the march, organisers said, adding that they did not want to publicise his identity until after the event.\n\nDozens of human rights activists held banners that said \"We will never forget the genocide in Srebrenica\" and the number \"8372\" referring to the number of victims.\n\nIn May, the United Nations approved a resolution establishing an international day of reflection and commemoration of the Srebrenica genocide, when Bosnian Serb forces killed more than 8,000 Bosniak men and boys over the course of three days in July 1995.\n\nThe vote in the 193-member General Assembly was 84-19, with 68 nations abstaining. Neighbouring Serbia was vehemently against the resolution, claiming the events in Srebrenica were not genocide but a \"terrible crime\".\n\nThe Srebrenica genocide remains among the worst atrocities committed during the Yugoslav dissolution wars of the 1990s.\n\nAfter 45 years of peace under President Josip Broz Tito's rule, Yugoslavia, comprised of six republics at the time, disintegrated in a series of wars that engulfed Slovenia, Croatia and Bosnia.\n\nIn Bosnia, the war saw the three main ethnic groups -- Bosnian Serbs, who are Eastern Orthodox, Catholic Bosnian Croats, and Bosniaks, who are Muslim -- pitted against each other along ethnic lines.\n\nOn July 11, 1995, Bosnian Serbs overran a UN-protected safe area in Srebrenica. They separated more than 8,000 Bosniak men and boys from their wives, mothers and sisters and slaughtered them. Those who tried to escape were chased through the woods and over the mountains around the ill-fated town.\n\nThe perpetrators then dumped their victims' bodies into hastily made mass graves, which they later dug up with bulldozers, scattering the remains among other burial sites to hide the evidence of their war crimes.\n\nThe Bosnian Serb wartime political leader Radovan Karad\u017ei\u0107 and his military commander Ratko Mladi\u0107 were both convicted of genocide in Srebrenica by a special UN war crimes tribunal in The Hague.\n\nIn all, the tribunal and courts in the Balkans have sentenced close to 50 Bosnian Serb wartime officials to more than 700 years in prison for the Srebrenica killings.\n\nHowever, a significant number of Serbian and Bosnian Serb officials still All three will attend the funeral.\n\nThe genocide, Europe's only acknowledged after World War II, occurred shortly after the break-up of then-Yugoslavia.\n\nOn July 11, 1995, Bosnian Serb forces overran the United Nations-protected safe area of Srebrenica, separating at least 8,000 Bosniak men and boys from their wives, mothers and sisters and slaughtered them.\n\nThose who tried to flee were relentlessly pursued through the forests and across the mountains surrounding Srebrenica.\n\nBasic, a historian, also said the international community was living through another atrocity with Israel's war on Gaza.\n\n\"The images we're seeing in Gaza today depict oppression and genocide inflicted upon the Palestinian people,\" he said.\n\n\"I wonder how the world has not learned from what happened in Srebrenica and Rwanda? How, in this modern day and age, some 30 years later, are we once again seeing history repeat itself?\"\n\nIn a post on X on Thursday, UN Secretary-General Antonio Guterres said he hoped the memory of Srebrenica would \"strengthen our collective resolve to build a world free from the scourge of genocide where justice and peace prevail\".\n\nIn 2007, the International Court of Justice (ICJ) in The Hague, the top UN court, characterised the crime in Srebrenica as genocide. Officials in Serbia and the Republika Srpska, the Serb entity in Bosnia, have continued to deny that a genocide occurred.\n\nBosnian Serb wartime political leader Radovan Karadzic and his military commander, Ratko Mladic, were both convicted of and sentenced for the genocide in Srebrenica by a special UN war crimes tribunal in The Hague.\n\nIn all, the tribunal and courts in the Balkans have sentenced close to 50 Bosnian Serb wartime officials to more than 700 years in prison for the genocide.\n\nYet, many who are believed to have committed or were involved in the genocide have not been prosecuted.\n\nOmer Hasanovic, another genocide survivor, told Al Jazeera that several of them continue to hold political positions in Republika Srpska.\n\n\"In 2003, the Srebrenica Commission compiled a list of 810 individuals known or suspected to have participated in the genocide ... but to this day, dozens from that list have yet to be legally prosecuted. He was 68 when he went missing in the summer of 1995 in the town of Zepa. My mother and father's cousins and many of our neighbors lost their lives in the genocide,\" said Hodzic, adding that two of her uncle's six sons managed to pass to the safe zone in Srebrenica.\n\nDutch troops responsible for protecting people in the UN zone failed to act when Serb forces occupied it on July 11, killing 2,000 men and boys in a single day.\n\nAbout 15,000 Bosniaks fled to the surrounding mountains, but Serb troops hunted them down and killed 6,000 more people.\n\nSerbs who allowed women and children to reach the region controlled by Bosnian soldiers massacred at least 8,372 Bosnian men in forest areas, factories, and warehouses. The murdered Bosnians were buried in mass graves.\n\nHodzic then fled to Germany, where she lived as a refugee with her children.\n\n\"When I was in Germany, I watched what happened in Srebrenica on television. It was a very difficult time. I was in contact with my sister, who lived in the city of Tuzla. My sister went to the area where the survivors of Srebrenica were brought and found my mother, sister-in-law, and her children,\" she said.\n\nHowever, Hodzic's father and brother were killed. Their body remains were found in a mass grave in Zvornik in 1996 and they were both buried in the Potocari Memorial Cemetery in Srebrenica.\n\nWhile 6,751 victims have been buried in the Potocari Memorial Cemetery to date, 250 have been buried in local cemeteries at the request of their families. More than 1,000 victims of the Srebrenica genocide have not been found.\n\nIn 2007, the International Court of Justice in The Hague ruled that a genocide was committed in Srebrenica.\n\nAmid efforts to find the missing after the war, victims whose bodies were found in mass graves are buried in a ceremony held at the Potocari Memorial Cemetery every year on July 11 after identification.\n\n\"Before the war, our father was working. There was always a happy atmosphere in our house. I always remember those beautiful moments. I always dream of running away from the Chetniks. Every year, when the funeral prayers are held, I come back to what we experienced that day. It is very difficult,\" she said.\n\nMekanic said she was captured by the Serbs twice during that period and her husband was killed while going to Srebrenica with a military unit to defend the city.\n\nMekanic said that victims' relatives can never forget the pain they felt.\n\n\"I cried a lot when they burned our house. But when I saw people being killed, I saw that the house had no meaning,\" she said.\n\nShe added that she remembers her father when she sees elderly people walking on the street.\n\n\"My father could have been like that too, but he is no longer there,\" she said.\n\nOn June 8, 2021, UN tribunal judges upheld a verdict sentencing Mladic to life in prison for genocide, persecution, crimes against humanity, extermination, and other war crimes committed in Bosnia and Herzegovina.\n\nOn this year's anniversary of the Srebrenica genocide, 14 more genocide victims who have been identified will be recognise the resolution.\n\nA UN court sentenced Bosnian Serb wartime political leader Radovan Karadzic and his army chief Ratko Mladic to life in prison for war crimes including the Srebrenica genocide.\n\nIncomplete remains\n\nOn Thursday, the remains of 14 more victims of the bloodshed, including a 17 year old boy, will be buried at a memorial cemetery in Potocari, just outside Srebrenica.\n\nBeriz Mujic, whose remains were found in the Srebrenica region last year, will be laid to rest next to his brother Hazim.\n\nSo far, the remains, often incomplete, of 6,988 Srebrenica victims have been buried, the overwhelming majority of them under white tombstones in Potocari.\n\nThe remains were found in 87 mass graves, and a spokeswoman for Bosnia's institute for missing persons told AFP that they are still looking for around 1,000 people.\n\nTo cover up the crime, Bosnian Serb forces moved the bodies of the victims to so called secondary mass graves.\n\nOn Wednesday, the European Union, which Bosnia aspires to join, called the atrocity \"one of the darkest moments in modern European history\".\n\n\"There is no place amongst us for those who deny genocide, attempt to rewrite history, and glorify war criminals,\" EU foreign policy chief Josep Borrell and EU enlargement commissioner Oliver Varhelyi said in a joint statement.\n\nThe annual commemoration ceremonies started on Monday with a 100 kilometre (62-mile) march towards Srebrenica.\n\nSeveral thousand people joined the march from the village of Nezuk, where the first survivors arrived days after the massacre.\n\nBosnia's 1992-1995 war between its Croats, Muslims and Serbs claimed approximately 100,000 lives.\n\nNearly three decades after the war ended, the Balkan nation remains deeply divided "sim": 0.7411764860153198, "url": "https://www.aa.com.tr/en/europe/bosnian-war-survivors-recall-painful-memories/3271193", "title": "Bosnian war survivors recall painful memories", "body": "Sisters Fatima Mekanic and Mulija Selimovic Hodzic say that every year, when funeral prayers are held for victims of the Srebrenica genocide, they go back in time 29 years\n\nSurvivors of the Bosnian war and relatives of victims of the Srebrenica genocide recounted their painful memories of the conflict to Anadolu on the 29th anniversary of the genocide, in which more than 8,000 people were killed.\n\nOn Dec. 21, 1991, Bosnian Serbs proclaimed their own republic after voting against independence from Yugoslavia in a referendum.\n\nOn Jan. 9, 1992, they proclaimed the Republic of the Serbian People in Bosnia-Herzegovina but did not officially declare independence.\n\nBosnia and Herzegovina declared independence after a referendum held on Feb. 29 and March 1, 1992 which sparked a three-year war.\n\nThe war lasted until Dec. 14, 1995, and more than 100,000 people were killed and 2 million had to migrate.\n\nThe fate of approximately 7,000 people who disappeared during the war is still unknown.\n\nRelatives of the war victims cannot forget the pain of losing their loved ones, despite the 29 years that have passed.\n\nSisters Fatima Mekanic (60) and Mulija Selimovic Hodzic (58) told Anadolu about the painful days they lived through as they lost their father, brothers, and many relatives in the Srebrenica genocide.\n\nHodzic and her husband, together with their three children, were living in the city of Vlasenica up until Serb forces entered their region after the start of the war in 1992.\n\nShe said her husband, father-in-law, and four brothers-in-law were killed in Vlasenica, and her mother, father, two brothers, and daughter-in-law had to flee to Srebrenica, where there was a UN \"safe area.\"\n\n\"My uncle's grandchildren, my uncle, and my aunt's son were also killed there. My mother and father's cousins and many of our neighbors lost their lives in the genocide,\" said Hodzic, adding that two of her uncle's six sons managed to pass to the safe zone in Srebrenica.\n\nThe UN Security Council declared Srebrenica a \"safe area\" in the spring of 1993. But Serb troops led by Gen. Ratko Mladic -- who was later found guilty of war crimes, crimes against humanity, and genocide -- overran the UN zone.\n\nDutch troops responsible for protecting people in the UN zone failed to act when Serb forces occupied it on July 11, killing 2,000 men and boys in a single day.\n\nAbout 15,000 Bosniaks fled to the surrounding mountains, but Serb troops hunted them down and killed 6,000 more people.\n\nSerbs who allowed women and children to reach the region controlled by Bosnian soldiers massacred at least 8,372 Bosnian men in forest areas, factories, and warehouses. The murdered Bosnians were buried in mass graves.\n\nThe bodies of genocide victims were discovered in 570 locations across the country, 77 of which were mass graves.\n\nHodzic then fled to Germany, where she lived as a refugee with her children.\n\n\"When I was in Germany, I watched what happened in Srebrenica on television. It was a very difficult time. I was in contact with my sister, who lived in the city of Tuzla. My sister went to the area where the survivors of Srebrenica were brought and found my mother, sister-in-law, and her children,\" she said.\n\nHowever, Hodzic's father and brother were killed. Their body remains were found in a mass grave in Zvornik in 1996 and they were both buried in the Potocari Memorial Cemetery in Srebrenica.\n\n\"The last time I went to Potocari, I read the (Muslim holy book of) Quran for my father and brother. I felt that something was pulling me to stay there. It is very difficult to explain that feeling in words for those who have not lost their loved ones,\" said Hodzic.\n\nWhile 6,751 victims have been buried in the Potocari Memorial Cemetery to date, 250 have been buried in local cemeteries at the request of their families. More than 1,000 victims of the Srebrenica genocide have not been found.\n\nIn 2007, the International Court of Justice in The Hague ruled that a genocide was committed in Srebrenica.\n\nAmid efforts to find the missing after the war, victims whose bodies were found in mass graves are buried in a ceremony held at the Potocari Memorial Cemetery every year on July 11 after identification.\n\nThe elder sister Mekanic, whose husband was killed in 1992, said they were very happy before the war.\n\n\"Before the war, our father was working. There was always a happy atmosphere in our house. I always remember those beautiful moments. I always dream of running away from the Chetniks. Every year, when the funeral prayers are held, I come back to what we experienced that day. It is very difficult,\" she said.\n\nMekanic said she was captured by the Serbs twice during that period and her husband was killed while going to Srebrenica with a military unit to defend the city.\n\n\"When I found my mother and sister, my mother was not well. She seemed lost. She did not hug me. I thought she did not miss me, but they said that my father and brother were taken away by the Serbs. My mother could not sleep for a long time, and when she told me what happened in Srebrenica, I understood why she could not sleep,\" she said.\n\nMekanic said that victims' relatives can never forget the pain they felt.\n\n\"I cried a lot when they burned our house. But when I saw people being killed, I saw that the house had no meaning,\" she said.\n\nShe added that she remembers her father when she sees elderly people walking on the street.\n\n\"My father could have been like that too, but he is no longer there,\" she said.\n\nOn June 8, 2021, UN tribunal judges upheld a verdict sentencing Mladic to life in prison for genocide, persecution, crimes against humanity, extermination, and other war crimes committed in Bosnia and Herzegovina.\n\nOn this year's anniversary of the Srebrenica genocide, 14 more genocide victims who have been identified will be 1995 genocide.\n\nEvery year on July 11, newly identified victims of the genocide are buried in a memorial cemetery in Potocari, located in the country's east.\n\nIn late May, the UN General Assembly passed a resolution designating July 11 as Srebrenica Genocide Remembrance Day, which received overwhelming support.\n\nThe resolution, spearheaded by Germany and co-sponsored by more than 40 countries, calls for July 11 to be declared the \"International Day of Reflection and Commemoration of the 1995 Genocide in Srebrenica.\"\n\nThe youngest victim to be buried this year is Beriz Mujic,
