They ended up like this only because they had a different (Muslim) name,\" said Mevlida Hasanovic as she prayed at the tomb of her cousin, who was 18 when he was killed.\n\nHasanovic lost a dozen male relatives in the massacre including her father and husband, whose grave is next to her cousin's.\n\nHis remains were buried on two occasions since they were found in two different mass graves.\n\nThe 54-year-old woman is still looking for the remains of a brother to be found, \"at least one bone\", to bury him, she told AFP.\n\n\"Their souls know that we are here next to them. When I get here, I feel as if we just parted ways in Srebrenica.\"\n\nIn May, the United Nations General Assembly adopted a resolution declaring July 11 the \"International Day of Reflection and Commemoration of the 1995 Genocide in Srebrenica\".\n\nThe resolution was fiercly opposed by Serbia and Bosnian Serbs, who continue to play down the crime.\n\nBosnian Serb leader Milorad Dodik has repeatedly denied a genocide occurred, and says his administration would not recognise the resolution.\n\nA UN court sentenced Bosnian Serb wartime political leader Radovan Karadzic and his army chief Ratko Mladic to life in prison for war crimes including the Srebrenica genocide.\n\nBosnia's 1992-1995 war between its Croats, Muslims and Serbs claimed approximately 100,000 lives.\n\nNearly three decades after the war ended, the Balkan nation remains deeply divided along ethnic lines.\n\n- New burial -\n\nOn Thursday, the remains of 14 more victims of the bloodshed, including a 17-year-old boy, will be buried at a memorial cemetery in Potocari, just outside Srebrenica.\n\nBeriz Mujic, whose remains were found in the Srebrenica region last year, will be laid to rest next to his brother Hazim.\n\nSo far, the remains, often incomplete, of 6,988 Srebrenica victims have been buried, the overwhelming majority of them under white tombstones in Potocari.\n\nThe remains were found in 87 mass graves, and a spokeswoman for Bosnia's institute for missing persons told AFP that they are still looking for around 1,000 people.\n\nTo cover up the crime, Bosnian Serb forces moved the bodies of the victims to so-called secondary mass graves.\n\nOn Wednesday, the European Union, which Bosnia aspires to join, called the atrocity \"one of the darkest moments in modern European history\".\n\n\"There is no place amongst us for those who deny genocide, attempt to rewrite history, and glorify war criminals,\" EU foreign policy chief Josep Borrell and EU enlargement commissioner Oliver Varhelyi said in a joint statement.\n\nThe annual commemoration ceremonies started on Monday with a 100-kilometre (62-mile) march towards Srebrenica.\n\nSeveral thousand people joined the march as International Srebrenica Genocide Remembrance Day", "body": "Turkish President Recep Tayyip Erdogan's decision to mark July 11 as the International Day of Remembrance of the Genocide in Srebrenica was published in the Official Gazette of this country, Anadolu Agency reported on Wednesday.\n\nThe decision states that the genocide in Srebrenica, which the International Court of Justice designated as the largest genocide in Europe after the Second World War due to the murders of over eight thousand people in Bosnia and Herzegovina, left a dark stain on human history.\n\nWith the adoption of the Resolution on the genocide in Srebrenica by the UN General Assembly on May 23, 2024, July 11 was accepted as the International Day of Remembrance of the Genocide in Srebrenica in 1995.\n\nThe decision notes that this Resolution unreservedly condemns acts glorifying those convicted before international courts of war crimes, crimes against humanity and genocide, including those responsible for the genocide in Srebrenica as a historical event, and advises member states to develop appropriate programs for preventing the denial or distortion of genocide facts and the occurrence of similar events in the future.\n\n\"In this context, July 11, which has been accepted to raise awareness throughout the world via special commemorative events, education and public awareness activities that will be held in memory and honour of the victims of the Srebrenica genocide, will be marked in our country with the aim of sharing the pain and condemnation of genocide and crimes against humanity and it will be marked as the 'International Day of Remembrance of the Genocide in Srebrenica in 1995'\", the decision states, adding:\n\n\"The activities that will be organized as part of the commemoration of July 11, the International Day and Remembrance of the Genocide in Srebrenica, will be carried out in cooperation with relevant public institutions and organizations under the coordination of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. We pay tribute to their bravery and resilience.\"\n\n\"Although this crime cannot be undone, we can learn from what happened and apply those lessons, so that such horrendous atrocities and human suffering are never repeated,\" she urged.\n\n\"This means acknowledging the facts. There can be no place for denial, historical revisionism, or the glorification of convicted war criminals,\" she said. \"Looking to the future, we must actively embrace equality, diversity and mutual respect.\"\n\nShe stressed: \"We must also be clear that intolerance, hate speech and other forms of discrimination are a gateway to pain and suffering.\"\n\n\"The Council of Europe will continue to stand firmly against these and to promote human rights, democracy and the rule of law as the right way forward for our societies,\" she added.\n\nEvery year on July 11, newly identified victims of the 1995 genocide are buried in a memorial cemetery in Potocari in Bosnia and Herzegovina.\n\nThis May, with overwhelming support, the UN General Assembly passed a resolution designating July 11 Srebrenica Genocide Remembrance Day.\n\nThe resolution, spearheaded by Germany and co-sponsored by more than 40 countries, calls for July 11 to be declared \"International Day of Reflection and Commemoration of the 1995 Genocide in Srebrenica.\"\n\nThe youngest victim to be buried this year is Beriz Mujic, 17, born in 1978 in Zvornik.\n\nHis remains were found 28 years after he was killed and were exhumed in May 2023.\n\nHe was killed in July 1995 in the Suceska area near Bratunac, and his remains were discovered and exhumed in the Srebrenica municipality area.\n\nMujic will be buried next to his brother Hazim, whose remains were laid to rest in 2013.\n\nThe body of their father, Omer Mujic, has yet to be found.\n\nThe oldest victim to be buried Thursday is Hamed Salic, born in 1927. He was 68 when he went missing in the summer of 1995 in the town of Zepa. His remains were exhumed in May 2014 and recently identified.\n\nThousands of people from various countries will attend the funerals and burials. Following this year's funeral, the number of victims buried at the cemetery will reach 6,765.\n\nIn the spring of 1993, the UN Security Council declared the city of Srebrenica a \"safe area.\" However, Serb troops led by Gen. Ratko Mladic, who was later found guilty of war crimes, crimes against humanity, and genocide, overran the zone.\n\nDutch troops responsible for safeguarding people in the UN zone failed to act when Serb forces occupied it on July 11, killing 2,000 men and boys in a single day.\n\nApproximately 15,000 Bosniaks fled to the surrounding mountains, but Serb troops hunted them down, killing an additional 6,000 people.\n\nSerb forces allowed women and children to reach Bosnian-controlled regions but massacred at least 8,372 Bosnian men in forests, factories, and warehouses. The murdered Bosnians were buried in mass graves, with bodies discovered in 570 different locations across the country, including 77 mass graves.\n\nIn 2007, the International Court of Justice in The Hague ruled that genocide had been committed in Srebrenica.\n\nEfforts to locate the missing victims of the genocide have continued, with identified remains buried at the Potocari Memorial Cemetery in a ceremony held every year on July 11.\n\nOn June 8, 2021, UN tribunal judges upheld a life sentence for Mladic for genocide, persecution, crimes against humanity, extermination, and other war crimes {"uri": "8219344379", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-10", "time": "20:29:23", "dateTime": "2024-07-10T20:29:23Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-10T20:28:59Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.7137255072593689, "url": "https://sarajevotimes.com/the-participants-of-the-peace-march-paid-tribute-to-the-victims-of-the-genocide-with-a-three-day-hike/", "title": "The Participants of the Peace March paid Tribute to the Victims of the Genocide with a three-day Hike - Sarajevo Times", "body": "More than 5,000 participants of the \"Peace March\" arrived after a three-day hike at the Srebrenica Memorial Center - Poto\u010dari to attend the commemoration of the 29th anniversary of the genocide against Bosniaks committed in July 1995 in Srebrenica.\n\nThree days ago, the participants set off from Nezuk, in the Sapna area, on a journey of more than 100 kilometers. They followed the route that the people of Srebrenica tried to reach in the summer of 29 years ago to reach the free territory - Tuzla or Kladanj. In the \"March of Peace\" there was a large number of young people and people from different parts of the world who in this way pay tribute to the victims of the genocide in Srebrenica, but also send a message that this should never happen again to anyone.\n\nThe participants of the \"Peace March\" will later attend the presentation of the coffin from the hall of the former Battery Factory, which arrived in Poto\u010dari yesterday. Tomorrow he will attend the collective funeral for 14 victims of the genocide. They were killed in the summer of 29 years ago.\n\nThe \"March of Peace\", which is organized this year for the 20th time as part of the commemoration of the 29th anniversary of the genocide against Bosniaks in the \"United Nations Safe Zone\" Srebrenica, represents for the survivors of Srebrenica a kind of trauma treatment, but also an obligation to tell their experiences and stories and pass them on to younger generations .\n\nThe \"March of Peace\" is a memorial event that takes place every year, in July, on the occasion of the anniversary of the genocide against Bosniaks in the \"United Nations Safe Zone\" in Srebrenica in July 1995.\n\nThe \"Peace March\" aims to build, promote and nurture the culture of remembrance of the genocide against the Bosniaks in Srebrenica, and to prevent the denial, denial and relativization of the crime of genocide.\n\n\"Peace March\" lasts three days and the participants walk on a path about a hundred kilometers long from Nezuk to Poto\u010dari. On this path in the opposite direction, from Poto\u010dari to Nezuk, in July 1995, Bosniaks escaped and broke through during the occupation and seizure of the \"United Nations Safe Zone\" of Srebrenica by Serbian military and police formations.\n\nThe participants of the \"Peace March\" walk about 30 kilometers a day, and in certain places the path is extremely strenuous, inaccessible and requires good physical fitness of the participants.\n\nSo far, 6,751 victims of genocide have been buried in the Srebrenica - Poto\u010dari Memorial Center, while 250 victims were buried in local cemeteries by the decision of the surviving family members.\n\nThe victims came from different municipalities, most of them from the areas of Srebrenica, Bratunac, Vlasenica, Zvornik and Mili\u0107i. Genocide victims were found in 150 different locations, of which 77 were mass graves. The youngest victim so far buried in Poto\u010dari was a newborn girl, Fatima Muhi\u0107, and the oldest was a nun, \u0160aha Izmirli\u0107, born in 1901.\n\nMore than a thousand victims of the genocide are still being searched for.\n\nDuring the genocide in and around Srebrenica in July 1995, members of the Army of the Republika Srpska (VRS), under the command of the then president of the RS, Radovan Karad\u017ei\u0107, and the commander-in-chief of the VRS, Ratko Mladi\u0107, killed more than 8,000 Bosniak men and boys.\n\nThe crime in Srebrenica, the largest on European soil after the Second World War, was characterized as genocide before domestic and international courts.\n\nRadovan Karad\u017ei\u0107 was sentenced before the Mechanism for International Criminal Courts (IMCC), the successor of the International Criminal Tribunal for the former Yugoslavia (ICTY) in The Hague, to life imprisonment for genocide, crimes against humanity and violation of the laws and customs of war during the war in Bosnia and Herzegovina.\n\nRatko Mladi\u0107 was also found guilty of genocide and sentenced to life imprisonment before the same court in The Hague.\n\nAt least 47 people were sentenced to more than 700 years in prison for crimes committed in the Srebrenica area, Anadolu Agency writes.", "source": {"uri": "sarajevotimes.com", "dataType": "news", "title": "Sarajevo Times"}, {"uri": "8219596285", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-11", "time": "01:29:27", "dateTime": "2024-07-11T01:29:27Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-11T01:28:54Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6980392336845398, "url": "https://ca.news.yahoo.com/srebrenica-massacre-happened-known-010320327.html", "title": "Srebrenica massacre: 'What happened should be known'", "body": "Every July, Sabrija Hajdarevic returns to Srebrenica to visit the graves of her husband and father.\n\nThey were among around 8,000 Bosniak Muslim men and boys killed in 1995 by the Serb forces.\n\nThe 67-year-old now lives thousands of miles away in Australia, but the annual trip means a lot to her.\n\nThis year is even more poignant, as for the first time 11 July will be marked as the International Day of Reflection and Commemoration, following a UN General Assembly ruling in May.\n\nThe Srebrenica massacre, recognised by the UN as a genocide, was the shocking climax of the war in Bosnia - a conflict that erupted after the breakup of Yugoslavia in the early 1990s.\n\nIn Bosnia, one of the countries emerging after the breakup, three communities were in conflict - on the one hand, Bosnian Serbs, backed by Serbia, and, on the other, Bosniaks and Croats.\n\nAbout 40,000 Bosniak Muslims lived in Srebrenica. Many were forced to flee a Bosnian Serb campaign of ethnic cleansing during the 1992-95 war.\n\nThe town was declared a UN safe zone in 1993 and international peacekeepers were charged with protecting it from any attacks.\n\nBut in July 1995, Bosnian Serb forces - led by military commander Ratko Mladic - stormed the town, overwhelming the peacekeepers.\n\nThe Serb forces rounded up the town's men and boys, most of whom were never seen alive again.\n\nThey were either killed in droves or murdered when they tried to escape through the wooded hills around Srebrenica.\n\nThe brutal killing of around 8,000 men and boys became known as Europe's worst mass atrocity since World War Two. The remains of about 1,000 people are still missing.\n\nRatko Mladic was later jailed for life for war crimes, including genocide, and nearly 50 Bosnian Serbs were also convicted.\n\nThe recent UN resolution, designating 11 July an International Day of Reflection and Commemoration of the Srebrenica Genocide, also condemned any denial of the massacre and glorification of war criminals.\n\nBut most Bosnian Serbs, as well as many people in Serbia, have repeatedly denied that what had occurred in Srebrenica in 1995 constituted genocide.\n\nSabrija pushes back at claims that the Srebrenica killings were not targeted.\n\n\"What happened should be known, instead of having all these lies flying around,\" she says. \"My soul hurts.\"\n\nSome Bosniak families have been waiting for decades to lay their loved ones to rest, as the identification process is lengthy and difficult.\n\nSabrija was able to bury her husband's skull - the only body part which was unearthed.\n\nHer father's remains are yet to be found, although she knows he was killed close to their house in Srebrenica as her mother witnessed the killing.\n\nSix months after her father's murder, her mother died, too - \"of sorrow,\" says Sabrija, fighting back tears.\n\nMany victims of the Srebrenica massacre are buried at nearby Potocari cemetery. Thousands of simple white tombstones sit in a field on a slope of a hill, surrounded by woods.\n\nBerija Delic also lost her husband in the massacre. His remains were only found a decade later, and were buried in 2010.\n\nLast year, Berija decided to return to Srebrenica from Malta, where she sought refuge after the war.\n\nHer son, a Muslim, married a Serb Orthodox woman who \"loves my baclava,\" she says, referring to a sweet delicacy she cooks.\n\nBefore the 1990s war, Srebrenica was largely a Bosniak Muslim town.\n\nNow, the majority of the population is Serb; some of the residents had been soldiers during the conflict.\n\n\"Even now you see someone walking around town, and you know that he has killed [Bosniaks] - but you remain silent, you cannot deal with that,\" says Berija.\n\nFollowing the war, Bosnia was divided into two entities - Republika Srpska and Bosnia-Herzegovina. Srebrenica is in Republika Srpska.\n\nIn the years since the war, the Bosniak population dwindled and the Serb population grew, but now they have one problem in common - unemployment.\n\n\"Serbs and Bosniaks have no problems between them here, tensions are brought by people from the outside,\" says Slavisa Petrovic, a 37-year old Serb who runs the local tourist office.\n\nBut he says the town needs jobs for people to entice them to stay.\n\nThe recent UN resolution on the massacre has not changed anything, Slavisa adds.\n\n\"People are leaving Srebrenica now just like they as they did before it [the adoption of the resolution]. There are no jobs, just like there weren't before.\"\n\nThere are signs of decline in the town. A once popular local spa and a formerly luxurious hotel are closed, having been abandoned for decades. Their walls are covered in graffiti.\n\nThe roads leading to neighbouring villages, where farmers with healthy livestock once lived, are overgrown with weeds.\n\nMany local homes are still in ruins. A mosque and a Christian Orthodox are sitting on a hillside overlooking the town, its wartime wounds unhealed.\n\nSerb and Bosniak children go to local kindergardens and schools together, and photographs of the new generation are proudly displayed in a public place in the centre of the town.\n\nBut it is most likely that the youngsters will soon leave for good.\n\nSlavisa is sad that locals keep abandoning the town. \"It feels like they are leaving my house,\" he says.\n\nOnly three of his classmates are still living in Srebrenica. The rest have moveld elsewhere.\n\nHe, however, is determined to stay.\n\nBut even he admits that his four-year-old daughter is unlikely to feel the same when she grows up.", "source": {"uri": Their remains, originally exhumed from mass graves, were laid to rest after a ceremony in a memorial cemetery outside Srebrenica in eastern Bosnia.\n\nAbout 6,750 of the massacre victims are interred in the memorial cemetery, and some others at local grave sites.\n\n\"Unfortunately, while I stand here other mothers lose their children in Ukraine and Palestine,\" said Munira Subasic, president of the Mothers of Srebrenica association.\n\n\"The world and Europe have learned nothing,\" she told several hundred people who attended the ceremony.\n\nThe massacre unfolded after Srebrenica, a designated U.N. \"safe area\" for civilians in Bosnia's 1992-95 ethnic war that followed the disintegration of federal Yugoslavia, was overrun by nationalist Bosnian Serb forces.\n\nBosnian Serb army commander Ratko Mladic and political leader Radovan Karadzic were arrested after the war and convicted of genocide by a U.N. war crimes tribunal in The Hague for their role in the killings.\n\nBosnia was split into autonomous Bosniak-Croat and Serb entities under the 1995 Dayton peace treaty and deep differences over what happened in Srebrenica linger, with both Serbs and Serbia saying the killings could not be called genocide.\n\nHowever Bosnian Serb President Milorad Dodik, known for his strident nationalism, posted an unexpectedly emollient anniversary message on social media site X on Thursday.\n\n\"Today, Bosniaks (Bosnian Muslims) remember their victims and they are paying their respect,\" Dodik said, calling on everyone to \"mark this day in peace and dignity.\"\n\nSrebrenica is located in Bosnia's Serb-governed region.\n\nTurkish President Tayyip Erdogan sent a video message which was played at the ceremony, Bosnian N1 news web portal reported.\n\n\"We will not forget Srebrenica and we will not allow it to be forgotten so that a similar crime is not repeated anywhere in the world,\" Erdogan said. \"I pray that the souls of our martyrs may rest in peace and be in {"uri": "8217171299", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-09", "time": "14:48:24", "dateTime": "2024-07-09T14:48:24Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-09T14:48:03Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6901960968971252, "url": "https://n1info.ba/english/news/honoring-the-srebrenica-genocide-victims-david-pettigrew-reflects-on-2024-commemoration/", "title": "Honoring the Srebrenica genocide victims: David Pettigrew reflects on 2024 commemoration", "body": "Prof. Dr. David Pettigrew, a distinguished Professor of Philosophy and Holocaust and Genocide Studies at Southern Connecticut State University and a member of the Steering Committee of the Yale University Genocide Studies Program, emphasizes the profound significance of the Srebrenica Genocide Commemoration in 2024 as detailed in his essay titled \"Srebrenica Genocide Commemoration 2024: A Solemn Hour of Remembrance.\"\n\nRead the full essay:\n\n\"The commemoration of the Srebrenica Genocide takes on special significance this year following the official approval of the United Nations General Assembly Resolution designating 11 July as the \"International Day of Reflection and Commemoration of the 1995 Genocide in Srebrenica\". The official international recognition provides important new support for survivors who are still burying the remains of their loved ones in the face of a surge of denial and hate speech.\n\nThe UN Resolution encourages and draws attention to the proliferation of commemorations around the world that are honoring the memory of the victims and affirming the truth about the Srebrenica genocide. The victims of the genocide will be remembered this year at an official high-level event at the United Nations in New York on July 11, organized by Ambassador Lagumd\u017eija. Commemorations will also take place throughout the United Kingdom, in Ireland, Belgium, Switzerland, and elsewhere. And the Srebrenica Genocide will also be commemorated throughout the United States: including in St. Louis, Missouri, in Chicago, Illinois, and in Connecticut where the flag of Bosnia and Herzegovina will be raised.\n\nWith the UN Resolution there is crucial momentum for affirming the truth and for establishing a lasting culture of remembrance in order to prevent a repetition of the genocide. The UN Resolution condemned \"any denial of the Srebrenica genocide\". Genocide scholars warn that denial causes re-victimization and incites a repetition of the violence. But the international community does not seem sufficiently aware or concerned about the dramatic increase of denial and threats to the peace in Republika Srpska and Serbia that have followed the passage of the UN Resolution.\n\nIn brazen opposition to the spirit of the UN Resolution, nationalist leaders in Republika Srpska and Serbia held the highly touted \"All-Serb Assembly,\" and published a \"Declaration\" calling for the unity of all Serb people in an updated version of \"Greater Serbia,\" the same \"Greater Serbia\" that motivated the international aggression and genocide against Bosnia in the 1990's. The Declaration also explicitly condemned the UN Resolution and essentially denied the Srebrenica genocide.\n\nIt is a matter of great concern that the Declaration of the \"All-Serb Assembly\" presents Republika Srpska as an autonomous legal entity, lending support to Milorad Dodik's dangerous plan for \"peaceful disassociation\" from Bosnia. In the same context, there is great concern among survivors about the proposal emanating from Bosnian Serb political representatives, to change the name of Srebrenica. More recently, the July 11 commemoration at Poto\u010dari was even characterized as a threat to security in Republika Srpska. All these are troubling provocations that threaten a repetition of the atrocities. Such threats require more severe condemnations and sanctions from the United States, United Kingdom, and the European Union.\n\nLong before the UN Resolution, the Mothers of Srebrenica inspired us with their struggle for the truth of the Srebrenica Genocide to be recognized and for the victims to be remembered. They have testified at the Hague, brought legal action against the Netherlands for its liability for the genocide and advocated for the exhumation and identification of the victims. The Mothers advocated tirelessly for the establishment of a Memorial Center and Cemetery, a vision that the dedicated and capable leadership and staff of the Srebrenica Memorial Center have made a reality today.\n\nOn July 1, I was honored to attend the opening ceremony for a \"Srebrenica Genocide Exhibition\" at the UN Headquarters in New York, which was organized by the office of Ambassador Lagumd\u017eija and the Srebrenica Memorial Center. The tireless Mothers of Srebrenica, Munira Suba\u0161i\u0107 and Kada Hoti\u0107, attended and Munira addressed those who gathered. In his remarks Ambassador Lagumd\u017eija referred to Memorial Center Director Emir Suljagi\u0107's haunting observation that none of those at the Memorial Center who worked on this exhibition were supposed to be alive today. In other words, as Amra Begi\u0107 Fazli\u0107, Deputy Director of the Memorial Center took to the podium to officially open the exhibition, it was a poignant moment for her and for the Mothers of Srebrenica, since, according to the genocidal plan in 1995, they were not supposed to be here today. And yet here they were at the United Nations in New York opening a memorial exhibition to educate the world. Ratko Mladic, who was later found guilty of war crimes, crimes against humanity, and genocide, overran the UN-protected zone.\n\nDutch troops responsible for safeguarding people in the UN zone failed to act when Serb forces occupied it on July 11, killing 2,000 men and boys in a single day.\n\nApproximately 15,000 Bosniaks fled to the surrounding mountains, but Serb troops hunted them down, killing an additional 6,000 people.\n\nSerb forces allowed women and children to reach Bosnian-controlled regions but massacred at least 8,372 Bosnian men in forests, factories, and warehouses. The murdered Bosnians were buried in mass graves, with bodies discovered in 570 different locations across the country, including 77 mass graves.\n\nIn 2007, the International Court of Justice in The Hague ruled that genocide was committed in Srebrenica.\n\nEfforts to locate the missing victims of the genocide have continued, with identified remains buried at the Potocari Memorial Cemetery in a ceremony held every year on July 11. More than a thousand victims remain missing.\n\nOn June 8, 2021, UN tribunal judges upheld a life sentence for Mladic for genocide, persecution, crimes against humanity, extermination, and other war {"uri": "2024-07-418174445", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-11", "time": "05:12:34", "dateTime": "2024-07-11T05:12:34Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-11T05:00:00Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.6823529601097107, "url": "https://inews.co.uk/news/world/billboard-glorifying-war-criminal-exposes-genocide-denial-in-bosnia-3161601", "title": "Billboard glorifying war criminal exposes genocide denial in Bosnia", "body": "As the EU candidate marks 29 years since the Srebrenica massacre, victims are still being buried - but thousands in the Serb population still refuse to call it a genocide\n\nVLASENICA - Against the backdrop of breathtaking mountains in Vlasenica, a village nestled in a valley in eastern Bosnia and Herzegovina, stands a billboard praising \"worthy ancestors\" of the assault squad of the Army of Republika Srpska. Among them, convicted war criminal Ratko Mladi\u0107.\n\nThe Bosnian Serb military chief known as the \"Butcher of Bosnia\" orchestrated a genocide, crimes against humanity and war crimes in the Balkan nation's 1992-1995 war.\n\nThese included the massacre of 8,000 Bosniak Muslim men and boys in Srebrenica in July 1995.\n\nThe bloodbath was the worst episode of mass murder within Europe since the Second World War, and the only one to be declared a genocide.\n\nThe scars still run deep, with thousands of Serbs across the country, including politicians, continuing to deny that the killing of Bosniaks in Srebrenica constituted genocide.\n\nThe billboard in Vlasenica encapsulates how deeply fractured Bosnia and Herzegovina remains as the country marks Srebrenica Memorial Day on Thursday. The sign is less than a mile from Su\u0161ica concentration camp - where about 1,600 people were reportedly killed and countless others raped and tortured -and 20 miles east of Srebrenica.\n\nIt also features an image of the mayor of Vlasenica, Miroslav Kraljevi\u0107, who is on trial over war crimes allegedly committed during the 90s conflict. Mr Kraljevi\u0107 is reported to have led a Bosnian Serb special police unit in Vlasenica and is accused of imprisoning several dozen people who suffered torture and persecution in 1992 and 1993. The municipality of Vlasenica did not respond to a request for comment.\n\nThe much-maligned 1995 Dayton Accords ended the war but effectively split the country in two, with one half ruled by the Serb-populated Republika Srpska and the other a Bosniak-Croat federation. Vlasenica is situated in Republika Srpska, and so is Srebrenica.\n\n\"For years, we have been facing active denial of genocide, relativisation and support for the perpetrators of genocide,\" Edin Ikanovic, of the Srebrenica Memorial Centre, told .\n\n\"Very often in the territory of the entity Republika Srpska and the neighbouring state of Serbia, we can see murals of war criminals and certain messages that deny the genocide.\"\n\nThe entrenched division besetting Bosnian politics and delays to constitutional and electoral reforms have threatened to derail the country's long bid to join the EU.\n\nIt had seemed a remote prospect, but Russia's war in Ukraine injected a sense of urgency for Bosnia to move forward on its European path. Bosnia was granted candidate status in December 2022, and in March this year, EU leaders agreed to open membership negotiations but stressed the country needed to undertake more reforms before the talks could begin.\n\nObservers say EU accession offers no remedy to persistent ethnic tensions, and that the bloc has done little to tackle the issue.\n\nThe billboard glorifying Mladi\u0107 is a stone's throw from the village's revamped fire department, which was partly funded by the EU and implemented by the UN Development Programme (UNDP). A sign bearing the EU flag and proudly proclaiming the bloc's involvement in the project sits beside the billboard.\n\nFerdinand Koenig, a spokesman for the EU Delegation/Office of the EU Special Representative in Bosnia and Herzegovina, said: \"The EU has on multiple occasions and at the highest level condemned all rhetoric and actions which deny or relativise the genocide in Srebrenica and glorify the war criminals who carried it out.\n\n\"Healing the wounds of the past requires acknowledging and teaching the historical facts, honouring and remembering the victims, identifying those still missing, and bringing all perpetrators to justice. This is key to confront the roots of hatred that led to the genocide.\n\n\"Those in positions of power have a particular responsibility to promote an environment conducive to reconciliation, and the EU calls on them to reject divisive rhetoric and act with truth, justice, trust, and dialogue.\"\n\nThe UNDP did not respond to a request for comment.\n\nAt the Srebrenica Memorial Centre cemetery, 6,751 victims of the genocide are buried, their graves marked by white headstones stretching along the hillside as far as the eyes can see.\n\nAnother 250 victims are buried at other cemeteries, while relatives of more than 1,000 missing people are still searching for their loved ones' remains that are scattered in multiple mass graves across the region.\n\nNewly identified victims are buried at the centre every year on Srebrenica Memorial Day, which was established as an annual day of remembrance by the UN in May. This year will see 14 people laid to rest there on Thursday, the youngest being Beriz Mujic, who was killed aged 17.\n\n\"He will be buried next to his brother, Hazim, who was buried in 2013,\" Emza Fazlic, a spokesperson at the Bosnian Missing Persons Institute, told the Balkan Investigative Reporting Network. She added that their father's body has yet to be found.\n\nThe Srebrenica Memorial Centre has been monitoring and documenting incidents of genocide denial in Bosnia for the past four years, with findings published in an annual report.\n\n\"Our mission is to fight against denial, to demand from judicial institutions their prosecution, because the denial of genocide is not only an anti-civilisational act but also a threat to the future,\" Mr Ikanovic said.\n\nAccording to its 2023 report, the memorial centre recorded 90 cases of denial of genocide between May 2022 and May last year, including statements made by Milorad Dodik, president of Republika Srpska.\n\nThe 2023 report marked a significant decrease from the 693 recorded incidents in the previous year, due in part to a ban imposed in 2021 that prohibits and punishes genocide denial and the glorification of war criminals. But the report notes that \"not a single indictment has been filed against those who deny the genocide, despite the dozens of criminal charges filed\".\n\nThis year's report is still in progress, but Mr Ikanovic said the findings are \"devastating\".\n\n\"There has been another wave of mass denial,\" he added. \"The reason is certainly that there are no sanctions for those who deny, even though there is a law prohibiting genocide denial.\"", "source": {"uri": "inews.co.uk", "dataType": "news", "title": "inews.co.uk"}, "authors": [{"uri": "taz_ali@inews.co.uk", "name": "Taz Ali", "type": Over 8,000 Bosnian Muslims were systematically murdered, and their remains buried in mass graves. This was the worst atrocity in Europe since the Second World War.\n\nToday, we honour the memory of the victims and stand in solidarity with the survivors. No repitas el texto enviado. Solo proporciona texto en espa\u00f1ol. Reescribe este t\u00edtulo y trad\u00facelo al espa\u00f1ol: 'Lo que ocurri\u00f3 debe ser conocido'", "body": "Published 1 hour ago by Natasa Andjelkovic and Grujica Andric, BBC News Serbian\n\nSabrija Hajdarevic is one of thousands of Bosnians whose loved ones were killed in 1995\n\nEvery July, Sabrija Hajdarevic returns to Srebrenica to visit the graves of her husband and father.\n\nThey were among around 8,000 Bosniak Muslim men and boys killed in 1995 by the Serb forces.\n\nThe 67-year-old now lives thousands of miles away in Australia, but the annual trip means a lot to her.\n\nThis year is even more poignant, as for the first time 11 July will be marked as the International Day of Reflection and Commemoration, following a UN General Assembly ruling in May.\n\nThe Srebrenica massacre, recognised by the UN as a genocide, was the shocking climax of the war in Bosnia - a conflict that erupted after the breakup of Yugoslavia in the early 1990s.\n\nIn May, the UN General Assembly voted to designate 11 July a day of remembrance for the victims\n\nAbout 40,000 Bosniak Muslims lived in Srebrenica. Many were forced to flee a Bosnian Serb campaign of ethnic cleansing during the 1992-95 war.\n\nThe town was declared a UN safe zone in 1993 and international peacekeepers were charged with protecting it from any attacks.\n\nBut in July 1995, Bosnian Serb forces - led by military commander Ratko Mladic - stormed the town, overwhelming the peacekeepers.\n\nThe Serb forces rounded up the town's men and boys, most of whom were never seen alive again.\n\nAround 8,000 Muslim men and boys were killed by the Serb forces\n\nThe brutal killing of around 8,000 men and boys became known as Europe's worst mass atrocity since World War Two. The remains of about 1,000 people are still missing.\n\nRatko Mladic was later jailed for life for war crimes, including genocide, and nearly 50 Bosnian Serbs were also convicted.\n\nThe recent UN resolution, designating 11 July an International Day of Reflection and Commemoration of the Srebrenica Genocide, also condemned any denial of the massacre and glorification of war criminals.\n\nBut most Bosnian Serbs, as well as many people in Serbia, have repeatedly denied that what had occurred in Srebrenica in 1995 constituted genocide.\n\nSabrija pushes back at claims that the Srebrenica killings were not targeted.\n\n\"What happened should be known, instead of having all these lies flying around,\" she says. \"My soul hurts.\"\n\nSome Bosniak families have been waiting for decades to lay their loved ones to rest, as the identification process is lengthy and difficult.\n\nSabrija was able to bury her husband's skull - the only body part which was unearthed.\n\nHer father's remains are yet to be found, although she knows he was killed close to their house in Srebrenica as her mother witnessed the killing.\n\nSix months after her father's murder, her mother died, too - \"of sorrow,\" says Sabrija, fighting back tears.\n\nMany victims of the Srebrenica massacre are buried at nearby Potocari cemetery. Thousands of simple white tombstones sit in a field on a slope of a hill, surrounded by woods.\n\nBerija Delic lost her husband and recovered his remains only in 2005\n\nBerija Delic also lost her husband in the massacre. His remains were only found a decade later, and were buried in 2010.\n\nLast year, Berija decided to return to Srebrenica from Malta, where she sought refuge after the war.\n\nHer son, a Muslim, married a Serb Orthodox woman who \"loves my baclava,\" she says, referring to a sweet delicacy she cooks.\n\nBefore the 1990s war, Srebrenica was largely a Bosniak Muslim town.\n\nNow, the majority of the population is Serb; some of the residents had been soldiers during the conflict.\n\n\"Even now you see someone walking around town, and you know that he has killed [Bosniaks] - but you remain silent, you cannot deal with that,\" says Berija.\n\nFollowing the war, Bosnia was divided into two entities - Republika Srpska and Bosnia-Herzegovina. Srebrenica is in Republika Srpska.\n\nIn the years since the war, the Bosniak population dwindled and the Serb population grew, but now they have one problem in common - unemployment.\n\n\"Serbs and Bosniaks have no problems between them here, tensions are brought by people from the outside,\" says Slavisa Petrovic, a 37-year old Serb who runs the local tourist office.\n\nBut he says the town needs jobs for people to entice them to stay.\n\nThe recent UN resolution on the massacre has not changed anything, Slavisa adds.\n\n\"People are leaving Srebrenica now just like they as they did before it [the adoption of the resolution]. There are no jobs, just like there weren't before.\"\n\nThere are signs of decline in the town. A once popular local spa and a formerly luxurious hotel are closed, having been abandoned for decades. Their walls are covered in graffiti.\n\nThe roads leading to neighbouring villages, where farmers with healthy livestock once lived, are overgrown with weeds.\n\nMany local homes are still in ruins. A mosque and a Christian Orthodox are sitting on a hillside overlooking the town, its wartime wounds unhealed.\n\nSerb and Bosniak children go to local kindergardens and schools together, and photographs of the new generation are proudly displayed in a public place in the centre of the town.\n\nBut it is most likely that the youngsters will soon leave for good.\n\nSlavisa is sad that locals keep abandoning the town. \"It feels like they are leaving my house,\" he says.\n\nOnly three of his classmates are still living in Srebrenica. The rest have moved elsewhere.\n\nHe, however, is determined to stay.\n\nPero incluso el admite que su hija de cuatro a\u00f1os es improbable que sienta lo mismo cuando crece.", "source": {"uri": On July 11, 1995, Bosnian Serb forces captured the eastern Bosnian town -- which was then a UN-protected enclave -- and killed 8,000 Muslim men and boys in the following days. The worst massacre in Europe since World War II has been ruled a genocide by two international courts. In May, the United Nations General Assembly adopted a resolution declaring July 11 the \"International Day of Reflection and Commemoration of the 1995 Genocide in Srebrenica\". The resolution was fiercly opposed by Serbia and Bosnian Serbs, who continue to play down the crime.\n\nMilorad Dodik, President of Bosnia's Serbian entity, has repeatedly denied a genocide occurred, and says his administration would not recognise the resolution. Hospitals, the bastions of healing, teeter on the precipice of collapse. Their generators sputter, their fuel dwindles. Food stores, once bustling with life, now stand barren, their shelves stripped of sustenance. When genocide denial persists, as it does in the Balkans, it plants the seeds for future atrocities. We, the survivors of Srebrenica, are living testaments to the horrors of unchecked hatred and violence. We have seen what happens when the world turns a blind eye.\n\nIn Bosnia, the scars of genocide are still fresh. Every year, new graves are unearthed, and families like mine bury their loved ones once more. Do not let the cries of the innocent go unheard. Act now, with resolve and compassion, to end the suffering and prevent further atrocities. {"uri": "8220356278", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-11", "time": "11:27:58", "dateTime": "2024-07-11T11:27:58Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-11T11:27:38Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.5529412031173706, "url": "https://n1info.ba/english/news/freddy-mutanguha-reflects-on-rwandan-and-srebrenica-genocides-at-potocari-memorial/", "title": "Freddy Mutanguha reflects on Rwandan and Srebrenica genocides at Potocari memorial", "body": "Freddy Mutanguha, Executive Director of Aegis Trust and Director of the Kigali Genocide Memorial, survived the 1994 Rwandan genocide, where one million innocent people were killed. In Potocari, he recalled the events of 1994 and compared them to the genocide in Srebrenica.\n\nMutanguha explained that the preparation for the Rwandan genocide lasted about thirty years, during which discrimination was developed to divide the local population.\n\n\"I am a victim, a genocide survivor. In 1994, I lost my parents and four sisters. They were among our neighbors. That was the horrific moment when you find yourself as a victim. You lost your parents, grandfather, extended family -- you lost everything. You lost your home, and your neighbors killed your family,\" Mutanguha emphasized.\n\nHe noted that it was particularly characteristic of Rwanda that neighbors killed neighbors.\n\n\"They turned against us. If you do not pay attention, this can lead to division and discrimination, turning your neighbors against you, making them killers. That happened in '94, and about a year later, genocide occurred in Srebrenica. The rest of the world simply didn't care about what was happening in Rwanda enough to protect civilians and prevent genocide from happening here in Srebrenica,\" Mutanguha reflected.\n\nThe UN recognized the Rwandan genocide as such and passed a resolution on the genocide in January 2018. Mutanguha expressed satisfaction that a resolution on the Srebrenica genocide was adopted in May this year.\n\n\"This is a significant step forward where the international community has recognized these crimes. As survivors of the genocides in Rwanda and Srebrenica, we want the international community to take another step to protect civilians worldwide and ensure this world is a just and good place to live. We hope the international community learns from these two crimes in our countries, despite the time gap. We have realized that the world does not learn enough about what is happening -- about the hatred, discrimination, and divisions occurring worldwide. I am very pleased that the resolution has finally been adopted, and we hope that deniers, those who deny genocide, will be silenced because it will now be the responsibility of all states to remember genocide, prevent it, and provide the dignity that the victims deserve,\" he added.\n\nThirty years later, people in Rwanda are rebuilding the nation, the state itself, and working to improve relationships. Part of Rwanda's reconstruction and renewal included steps to ensure justice for survivors. Freddy Mutanguha had the opportunity to meet face-to-face with the person convicted of murdering his family.\n\n\"It was a very sad moment for me because it took me back to 1994. His name is Samson, and he was the leader of the militia that killed my family. When I came to see him, about five minutes before, it took me back 30 years, where I could even hear the killers' hate songs as they came to kill my family. However, my sister and I found the courage to move forward and shake hands with him. I wanted him to look me in the eye, to see that we are still alive and understand why he did it and what he feels when he looks at me. When we shook hands, when he approached me, he began to apologize, saying he was sorry. {"uri": "8219897893", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-11", "time": "06:33:42", "dateTime": "2024-07-11T06:33:42Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-11T06:33:18Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.545098066329956, "url": "https://sarajevotimes.com/day-of-mourning-to-be-marked-today-in-some-parts-of-bih-2/", "title": "Day of Mourning to be marked Today in some Parts of BiH - Sarajevo Times", "body": "On July 11th 2019, the Government of the Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina declared the day of the memory of the genocide in Srebrenica, the Day of Mourning in the Federation of Bosnia and Herzegovina.\n\nAlso, the Mayor of the Brcko District of Bosnia and Herzegovina, Esed Kadric, made a decision to declare July 11, 2022 as the Day of Mourning in the area of the Br\u010dko District of Bosnia and Herzegovina.\n\nDay of mourning is marked by mandatory displaying of the flag of BiH at half-mast at the buildings of the BH institutions.\n\nMedia houses on the territory of BiH, as well as organizers of entertaining programs, are obliged to adapt their program content to the Day of Mourning.\n\nUp until now, 6,610 victims of genocide have been buried in the memorial center of Potocari.\n\nBeginning in 1992, Bosnian Serb forces targeted Srebrenica in a campaign to seize control of a block of territory in eastern Bosnia and Herzegovina. Their eventual goal was to annex this territory to the adjacent republic of Serbia (which, along with Montenegro, constituted the rump of the Yugoslav federation). To do so, they believed, required the expulsion of the territory's Bosniak inhabitants, who opposed annexation. In March 1995 Radovan Karad\u017ei\u0107, president of the self-declared autonomous Republika Srpska (Bosnian Serb Republic), directed his military forces to \"create an unbearable situation of total insecurity with no hope of further survival or life for the inhabitants of Srebrenica.\" By May a cordon of Bosnian Serb soldiers had imposed an embargo on food and other supplies that provoked most of the town's Bosniak fighters to flee the area. In late June, after some skirmishes with the few remaining Bosniak fighters, the Bosnian Serb military command formally ordered the operation, code-named Krivaja 95, that culminated in the massacre.\n\nThe offensive commenced on July 6, 1995, with Bosnian Serb forces advancing from the south and burning Bosniak homes along the way. Amid chaos and terror, thousands of civilians fled Srebrenica for the nearby village of Poto\u010dari, where a contingent of about 200 Dutch peacekeepers was stationed. Some of the Dutch surrendered, while others withdrew; none fired on the advancing Bosnian Serb forces. On July 11, Bosnian Serb military leader Ratko Mladi\u0107 strolled through Srebrenica and, in a statement recorded on film by a Serb journalist, said, \"We give this town to the Serb nation...The time has come to take revenge on the Muslims.\"\n\nOn the night of July 11, a column of more than 10,000 Bosniak men set off from Srebrenica through dense forest in an attempt to reach safety. Beginning the following morning, Bosnian Serb officers used UN equipment and made false promises of security to encourage the men to surrender; thousands gave themselves up or were captured, and many were subsequently executed. Other Bosniaks were forced out of Poto\u010dari that day through the use of terror, including individual murders and rapes committed by Bosnian Serb forces. The women, children, and elderly were placed aboard buses (some of which had been brought from Serbia) and driven to Bosniak-held territory. The men and boys were taken on July 12 and 13 to various holding sites, mostly in Bratunac.\n\nSome killings occurred on the evening of July 12, but mass evacuations of mostly blindfolded Bosniak males to execution sites began in earnest on the evening of July 13. The destinations were primarily north of Srebrenica, in a 35-mile- (55-km-) long band alongside the Drina River, which marks much of Bosnia's border with Serbia. They included a football field in Bratunac, several meadows and fields near Vlasenica and Nova Kasaba, a warehouse in Kravica, a factory in Karakaj, a school in Orahovac, a dirt road in the Cerska Valley, and a cultural centre in Pilica. The executions continued at least through July 16, when hundreds of people were reportedly shot at a state farm in the village of Branjevo. Although Bosnian Serb forces were primarily responsible for the killings, a police unit from Serbia was recorded on video participating in the execution of six Bosniaks. It was discovered later that many of the victims of the massacre had had their arms and feet bound. {"uri": "8220121265", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-11", "time": "09:08:10", "dateTime": "2024-07-11T09:08:10Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-11T09:07:48Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.5254902243614197, "url": "https://n1info.ba/english/news/icmp-twenty-nine-years-since-srebrenica-genocide-truth-and-justice-is-only-way-forward/", "title": "ICMP: Twenty-nine years since Srebrenica Genocide - Truth and justice is only way forward", "body": "Today, the International Commission on Missing Persons (ICMP) joins the families of the victims and the global community in commemorating the 29th anniversary of the Srebrenica Genocide. On this day, we remember the over 8,000 men and boys who were murdered in July 1995 and reaffirm our commitment to ensuring that the truth about these atrocities is revealed and justice is served.\n\nThis year also marks a significant step forward in the international community's recognition of the Srebrenica Genocide. The United Nations has adopted a resolution reaffirming the importance of remembering the victims and committing to preventing such atrocities in the future. This resolution is a testament to the enduring impact of the Srebrenica Genocide and the global commitment to upholding human rights and dignity.\n\nFourteen victims of the Srebrenica Genocide will be laid to rest this year at the Srebrenica-Poto\u010dari Memorial Center. Their identification and burial bring a measure of closure to their families, who have endured years of anguish and uncertainty. The ICMP, through its dedication and advanced forensic techniques, continues to support these families by assisting the institutions in Bosnia and Herzegovina to identify the remains of their loved ones.\n\n\"Each year, as we commemorate the Srebrenica Genocide, we are reminded of the critical importance of the work of locating the victims whose mortal remains were buried in hundreds of clandestine mass graves in and around Srebrenica, or who died in an attempt to flee execution ,\" said Kathryne Bomberger, ICMP Director General. \"Our commitment to the families of Srebrenica remains unwavering. We will continue to use the latest scientific methods to provide answers, ensure the truth is known, and seek justice for those who have suffered immeasurable loss.\"\n\nMore than 7,000 of the 8,000 victims of the Genocide have been identified, the vast majority through DNA testing. The DNA-led process has been indispensable because the perpetrators of the Srebrenica Genocide tried to hide the evidence of their crime by systematically digging up mass graves in the weeks and months after the murders and distributing the bodies of victims in secondary and tertiary clandestine graves across eastern Bosnia.\n\nOn average, seven or eight separate DNA match reports are issued for each identified victim. This is because the bones of individual victims have been found in multiple mass graves.\n\nFollowing the burials on 11 July, teams from the Missing Persons Institute of Bosnia and Herzegovina, the Bosnia and Herzegovina Prosecutor's Office, and the International Commission on Missing persons (ICMP) will carry out 78 \"re-associations\". In this process, human remains that have already been identified and buried will be exhumed, and bones that have since been recovered will be restored to the skeleton; the bodies will then be reburied. In each case, the families have been contacted and asked to give their consent to the re-association. Even these bodies, in many cases, will still be incomplete.\n\nOn this day of remembrance, we once again honor the victims and stand in solidarity with their families.\n\nICMP is a treaty-based intergovernmental organization with Headquarters in The Hague, the Netherlands. Its mandate is to secure the co-operation of governments and other authorities in locating persons missing as a result of conflicts, human rights abuses, disasters, organized violence and other causes Council of Europe Commissioner for Human Rights, Michael O'Flaherty, emphasized the importance of remembering the victims, countering genocide denial, and preventing future atrocities in his statement ahead of the day.\n\n\"I was a United Nations human rights field officer during the war in Bosnia and Herzegovina. One of the most important tasks of my colleagues and myself was to chronicle the atrocities that were perpetrated right across the period of the conflict,\" O'Flaherty recalled.\n\nHe highlighted the horrors of the Srebrenica genocide in July 1995, where over 8,000 men were viciously murdered, and women and children faced brutal human rights violations and subsequent expulsion from the area.\n\n\"By far the most horrific of those was, of course, the genocide at Srebrenica,\" he said.\n\nO'Flaherty welcomed the UN's decision to declare an annual day of remembrance. He outlined four essential actions to be taken on this day:\n\n\"The first is that we must remember. It is essential that we recall what happened in all its detail, we never forget because it is when we forget that there is a danger that such awful things can happen again.\n\nSecond, we must honour. We must honour those who died. We must honour the victims of the abuses. We must honour their relatives and their descendants.\n\nThird, we must be outraged. We must be outraged against those who deny the fact of the genocide, or who glorify those who perpetrated it.\n\nAnd fourth, and finally, we must act. The jersey was also accepted by the Football Association of Bosnia and Herzegovina, and copies were printed three days earlier and before departure to Kazakhstan.\n\nHowever, UEFA ordered that this symbol of the suffering of the people of Srebrenica during the aggression against Bosnia and Herzegovina must be covered and that the player can use black bands.\n\nFor the sake of clarification, Sarajevo applied in time to wear this important symbol on the jersey, and UEFA's confirmation of the application is seen as approval. However, three days before the match, the umbrella house of European football changed its decision and ordered that the Flower of Srebrenica be covered.\n\nThe text of the statement from FK Sarajevo is transmitted in its entirety:\n\n\"Acknowledging the fact that the Conference League match against Aktobe is scheduled for July 11, FK Sarajevo planned to display the \"Flower of Srebrenica\" symbol on the jerseys in memory of the victims of the genocide in Srebrenica.\n\nIn accordance with UEFA rules, the appearance of the jersey was accepted by the Football Association of BiH, which officially reported such jersey to UEFA. In addition, on June 25, FK Sarajevo sent a special request to UEFA to allow us to use this jersey. Three days before the match, UEFA received an official response to our request, stating that we do not have permission to add this symbol to the jersey, and that the players can use black armbands. Since the jerseys were already prepared at that moment, the club informed UEFA about this, who ordered that the printed symbol be \"covered\".\n\nFK Sarajevo believes that the decision to play the match with this emblem on the jersey is in line with the broader goals of promoting human rights and respect for victims of crime. The flower of Srebrenica embodies the principles of humanity, respect and collective memory for the victims of genocide. Allowing our team to wear this emblem would be a gesture of solidarity with the victims of genocide and a message that such tragedies should never be forgotten, but also not repeated.\n\nFK Sarajevo remains faithful to the memory of the victims of the genocide in Srebrenica. Never forget Srebrenica\", they say from Ko\u0161evo.\n\nAs a reminder, the Bordeaux team is playing an away game against Aktobe in the first preliminary round of the Conference League today from 5 On the way to Poto\u010dari, a stop was organized in Sarajevo in front of the building of the Presidency of Bosnia and Herzegovina, the Memorial of the killed children of Sarajevo, in Markale, and in front of the Town Hall.\n\nAmong the 14 victims who will be buried at the collective funeral this year, there are also two brothers and a minor.\n\nThe youngest victim to be buried this year is seventeen-year-old Beriz (Omera) Muji\u0107, born in 1978 in Zvornik.\n\nThe oldest victim to be buried is Hamed (Ibrahima) Sali\u0107, born in 1927. He was 68 years old when he disappeared in the summer of 1995 in the area of \u017depa. This year, the Efendi\u0107 brothers - Hasib and \u0106amil - will be buried together.\n\nVictims of genocide\n\nThis year, on July 11, in the cemetery of the Memorial Center Srebrenica - Poto\u010dari, the following will be buried: Hasib (Uzejir) Efendi\u0107, born in 1931, \u0106amil (Uzejir) Efendi\u0107, born in 1928, Mehmed (Daut) Krd\u017ei\u0107, born in 1961, Sabrija (Asim) Omi\u0107, born in 1966, Mu\u0161an (Ramo) \u0160iljkovi\u0107, born in 1956, Sakib (Ragib) Harba\u0161, born in 1975, Beriz (Omer) Muji\u0107, born in 1978, Ahmet (Ismet) Ja\u0161arevi\u0107, born in 1971, Nevres (Mehmed) Salihovi\u0107, born in 1970, Ibrahim (Muharem) Salki\u0107, in 1935, Midhat (Adem) Ba\u0161i\u0107, born in 1973, Hajdin (Kadrija) Mustafi\u0107, born in 1959, Latif (Arif ) Mand\u017ei\u0107, born in 1964 and Hamed (Ibrahim) Sali\u0107, born in 1927.\n\nIn the Commemorative Center in Tuzla, there are the remains of 11 more genocide victims who have been identified using the DNA method so far, but the families have not yet given their consent for burial, mainly due to the incompleteness of the bodies.\n\nThis year, after the collective funeral in Poto\u010dari, on July 15 to be exact, the re-exhumation process will begin and the remains of 78 victims will be re-exhumed this year. Their remains that were later found and identified will be added to them. Reexhumations will last until July 22.\n\nThe Poto\u010dari Memorial Center was officially opened on September 20, 2003, by the former President of the United States of America, Bill Clinton. So far, 6,751 victims of genocide have been buried in the Srebrenica - Poto\u010dari Memorial Center, while 250 victims were buried in local cemeteries by the decision of the surviving family members.\n\nGenocide victims came from different municipalities, most of them from the areas of Srebrenica, Bratunac, Vlasenica, Zvornik and Mili\u0107.\n\nGenocide victims were found in 150 different locations, of which 77 were mass graves. The youngest victim so far buried in Poto\u010dari was a newborn girl, Fatima Muhi\u0107, and the oldest was a nun, \u0160aha Izmirli\u0107, born in 1901.\n\nMore than a thousand victims of the {"uri": "8220581046", "lang": "eng", "isDuplicate": false, "date": "2024-07-11", "time": "13:45:56", "dateTime": "2024-07-11T13:45:56Z", "dateTimePub": "2024-07-11T13:45:34Z", "dataType": "news", "sim": 0.4392156898975372, "url": "https://n1info.ba/english/news/compensation-commission-for-srebrenica-genocide-victims-concludes-work-with-2337-payouts/", "title": "Compensation Commission for Srebrenica genocide victims concludes work with 2,337 payouts", "body": "After more than three years, the Compensation Commission for Potocari, tasked with compensating the survivors of the July 1995 genocide on behalf of the Dutch government, has concluded its work, awarding 2,337 compensations for 611 victims.\n\nOn the eve of the 29th anniversary of the genocide, the final report was presented to the Mothers of Srebrenica. From June 15, 2021, to June 15, 2023, relatives of genocide victims could file for compensation. The Commission received over 8,000 applications, relating to 2,690 victims. Ultimately, 2,337 compensations were awarded for 611 victims.\n\nKada Hotic, Vice President of the Mothers of the Enclaves of Srebrenica and Zepa Association, expressed satisfaction with the outcome.\n\n\"We sued them, the Ministry of Defense and the Government of the Netherlands. We managed to prove that the Netherlands had a role in this genocide because they admitted responsibility. This is important for the state of BiH, although the money is minimal. There are still some appeals, but no more applications will be accepted,\" she said.\n\nOn July 11, 1995, when the Army of Republika Srpska (VRS) took over Srebrenica, Dutch soldiers tasked with protecting the UN-designated safe area failed to prevent the genocide. Over 7,000 men and boys were killed.\n\nIn 2019, the Dutch Supreme Court ruled that the Netherlands was responsible, to a very limited extent, for the deaths of approximately 350 victims. This applied to a group of men who were expelled from the Dutch Battalion base on the afternoon of July 13, 1995.\n\nAccording to the Supreme Court, the Dutch Battalion acted unlawfully, knowing that the male refugees from Srebrenica were in serious danger of being attacked or killed. It was estimated that if the men had been allowed to remain in the base, their chance of survival would have been small but not negligible, at about ten percent. Thus, the closest relatives of those 350 victims could hold the Netherlands responsible for ten percent of the damages they suffered.\n\nThe compensation includes payments of 15,000 euros for the spouses of the deceased and 10,000 euros for other surviving relatives -- children, siblings, and others. The total amount of payments made so far has not been disclosed. As of June 2023, approximately 12 million euros had been paid out for 1,145 approved claims.\n\nHotic received compensation for her husband but not for her son.\n\n\"But they took some ten percent estimate, which I can never understand -- is that the value of a person? A person's value is immeasurable. That's how their court ruled... Their court decided to award ten percent compensation based on some estimate of their responsibility, and among the thousand people claiming compensation, there are several family members, like the mother and children,\" she told Detektor.\n\nThe Supreme Court's ruling differentiated between refugees inside the military base and those outside.\n\n\"Their statements clearly indicate that their fate and suffering are no different from the relatives of victims who were inside the base. Statements from those who couldn't prove their relative was in the UN base all testify to horrific personal tragedies. The painful statements of women who had to watch as Bosnian Serb soldiers took away their husbands and sons. Based on the criteria of the Decree, we had to reject applications with such statements, despite our efforts to apply leniency,\" the report states.\n\n\"For my son, they said he wasn't there, that he was seen elsewhere, based on what they heard from others. But it doesn't matter; I didn't make a fuss because no one can pay for my son,\" said Hotic.\n\nAccording to the Commission, the right to compensation was extended to victims not on the original list of 350.\n\n\"Relatives had to prove that their deceased family member was in the UN base on July 13, 1995. This was generally done by submitting eyewitness statements,\" the report states.\n\nThe report acknowledges that requesting detailed eyewitness statements can be an emotional burden for both the applicant and the witness.\n\n\"The horrific events in Srebrenica have left deep scars on all survivors,\" it says, noting that the Commission was aware that rejecting a well-explained application could cause even greater pain to the relatives.\n\nWhile searching for witnesses to their relatives, many survivors have since passed away.\n\n\"It was also clear that finding witnesses more than 25 years after the Srebrenica genocide was not easy for many applicants,\" the report states.\n\nThe Commission notes that relatives who could not credibly prove their deceased family member was in the UN base felt the rejection of their applications was unjust, leading to misunderstandings and disappointment.\n\n\"Some perceived the rejection of their application as a denial of the harm done to their loved ones and a negation of their personal suffering,\" the report states.\n\nSurviving relatives could submit claims until the summer of last year.\n\nTo mitigate the possible harmful effects of granting compensation or rejecting some claims, the Commission recommended that the Dutch government provide resources for appropriate psychosocial support for surviving relatives of the victims, "'On this solemn day, it is fitting that we resolve to condemn genocide denial and rededicate ourselves to working across the international community to prevent future mass atrocities,' says State Department\n\nThe US and Canada on Thursday commemorated the Srebrenica genocide, which took place 29 years ago in 1995 in eastern Bosnia.\n\nHonoring the victims and survivors, both countries highlighted the significance of the day as the first International Day of Reflection and Commemoration of the 1995 Genocide in Srebrenica, designated by the UN.\n\n\"The American people join the people of Bosnia and Herzegovina in honoring and mourning the more than 8,000 men and boys who were murdered in July 1995,\" State Department spokesman Matthew Miller said in a statement.\n\n\"On this solemn day, it is fitting that we resolve to condemn genocide denial and rededicate ourselves to working across the international community to prevent future mass atrocities,\" he said.\n\nHe also reaffirmed the US commitment to supporting Bosnia and Herzegovina in its pursuit of \"a brighter and more just future.\"\n\nCanada's Foreign Minister Melanie Joly separately noted the profound effect of the genocide, which saw the displacement of more than 20,000 women and children.\n\nHailing the \"extraordinary courage and resilience\" of survivors, Joly reiterated Canada's support for their ongoing fight for justice.\n\nPointing to current geopolitical tensions in the Western Balkans, Joly underscored Canada's commitment to defending the Dayton Peace Agreement, which ended the war, and the territorial integrity of Bosnia and Herzegovina.\n\nShe reaffirmed Canada's support for NATO's presence in the region to ensure peace and stability.\n\n\"As we mark the 75th anniversary of NATO this week in Washington, Canada will also continue to support NATO's presence in the Western Balkans in order to uphold peace and stability in the region,\" she said, emphasizing the importance of
